###begin article-title 0
###xml 88 98 88 98 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
A Ubiquitin Ligase Complex Regulates Caspase Activation During Sperm Differentiation in Drosophila
###end article-title 0
###begin article-title 1
A Protein Complex Restrains a Homicidal Enzyme during Sperm Differentiation
###end article-title 1
###begin p 2
###xml 116 126 116 126 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
###xml 670 676 670 676 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 714 724 714 724 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
###xml 1101 1107 1101 1107 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
In both insects and mammals, spermatids eliminate their bulk cytoplasm as they undergo terminal differentiation. In Drosophila, this process of dramatic cellular remodeling requires apoptotic proteins, including caspases. To gain further insight into the regulation of caspases, we screened a large collection of sterile male flies for mutants that block effector caspase activation at the onset of spermatid individualization. Here, we describe the identification and characterization of a testis-specific, Cullin-3-dependent ubiquitin ligase complex that is required for caspase activation in spermatids. Mutations in either a testis-specific isoform of Cullin-3 (Cul3Testis), the small RING protein Roc1b, or a Drosophila orthologue of the mammalian BTB-Kelch protein Klhl10 all reduce or eliminate effector caspase activation in spermatids. Importantly, all three genes encode proteins that can physically interact to form a ubiquitin ligase complex. Roc1b binds to the catalytic core of Cullin-3, and Klhl10 binds specifically to a unique testis-specific N-terminal Cullin-3 (TeNC) domain of Cul3Testis that is required for activation of effector caspase in spermatids. Finally, the BIR domain region of the giant inhibitor of apoptosis-like protein dBruce is sufficient to bind to Klhl10, which is consistent with the idea that dBruce is a substrate for the Cullin-3-based E3-ligase complex. These findings reveal a novel role of Cullin-based ubiquitin ligases in caspase regulation.
###end p 2
###begin title 3
Author Summary
###end title 3
###begin title 4

###end title 4
###begin p 5
###xml 802 812 802 812 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
###xml 1250 1254 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1259 1265 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">humans</span>
###xml 1335 1346 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">fruit flies</span>
###xml 1350 1356 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">humans</span>
Caspases are a family of proteases that play important roles in programmed cell death (apoptosis). These enzymes also have nonlethal functions, for example, in inflammation, cell differentiation, and cellular morphogenesis. During maturation, sperm cells eliminate the majority of their cytoplasm and organelles as they are transformed into highly specialized DNA delivery vehicles. Although caspase activation does not kill the entire cell in this case, sperm maturation resembles apoptosis in the sense that many cellular structures are degraded. An important unresolved question is how the lethal activity of apoptotic caspases is regulated to prevent the unwanted death of cells. Here, we show that a Cullin-3-based enzyme complex is required for caspase activation during sperm differentiation in Drosophila. Cullins are known to target cellular proteins for degradation, but their role in caspase regulation was not previously recognized. Our results suggest that a specific Cullin-3 enzyme complex activates caspases by degrading potent caspase inhibitors, thereby providing a model for how apoptotic proteins are regulated during cellular remodeling. Importantly, components of this Cullin-3 enzyme complex are also required for fertility in mice and humans, indicating that this mechanism has been conserved in evolution from fruit flies to humans.
###end p 5
###begin p 6
This work suggests that a specific Cullin-3 enzyme complex activates caspases by degrading potent caspase inhibitors.
###end p 6
###begin title 7
Introduction
###end title 7
###begin p 8
###xml 149 150 149 150 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b001">1</xref>
###xml 151 152 151 152 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b004">4</xref>
###xml 562 563 562 563 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b005">5</xref>
###xml 564 565 564 565 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b009">9</xref>
###xml 761 763 761 763 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b010">10</xref>
###xml 764 766 764 766 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b011">11</xref>
###xml 1254 1255 1250 1251 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b001">1</xref>
###xml 1256 1257 1252 1253 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b003">3</xref>
###xml 1258 1260 1254 1256 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b012">12</xref>
###xml 1261 1263 1257 1259 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b021">21</xref>
###xml 1624 1626 1620 1622 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b022">22</xref>
###xml 1627 1629 1623 1625 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b023">23</xref>
###xml 1736 1746 1732 1742 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
###xml 1748 1758 1744 1754 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
###xml 1888 1890 1884 1886 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b024">24</xref>
###xml 1891 1893 1887 1889 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b027">27</xref>
###xml 2169 2171 2165 2167 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b028">28</xref>
###xml 2172 2174 2168 2170 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b029">29</xref>
###xml 2299 2301 2295 2297 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b024">24</xref>
###xml 2302 2304 2298 2300 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b026">26</xref>
###xml 2305 2307 2301 2303 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b027">27</xref>
###xml 2438 2440 2434 2436 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b030">30</xref>
###xml 2557 2559 2553 2555 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b031">31</xref>
###xml 2671 2673 2667 2669 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b030">30</xref>
###xml 2674 2676 2670 2672 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b032">32</xref>
###xml 2677 2679 2673 2675 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b037">37</xref>
###xml 3026 3028 3022 3024 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b038">38</xref>
###xml 3029 3031 3025 3027 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b040">40</xref>
Caspases are a family of cysteine proteases that have received considerable attention because of their critical roles in inflammation and apoptosis [1-4]. Caspases are expressed as weakly active zymogens in virtually all cells of higher metazoans, and their conversion to the active enzyme is tightly controlled by many different signaling pathways. Historically, most efforts to understand the mechanism of caspase regulation have focused on activator proteins, such as Apaf-1 and FADD, which promote the assembly of active initiator caspase protein complexes [5-9]. Once activated, apoptotic initiator caspases cleave and activate effector caspases, which in turn cleave a variety of important cellular targets, thereby promoting the execution of cell death [10,11]. Given the widespread expression of pro-caspases that have the potential to auto-activate in a proteolytic cascade, one might expect that efficient mechanisms exist to prevent inappropriate caspase activation in cells that should live. Furthermore, activation of apoptotic effector caspases does not always result in cell death. For example, apoptotic caspases have been shown to play a critical role for cell differentiation, proliferation, NF-kappaB signaling, and dendritic pruning [1,3,12-21]. At this time, the mechanisms that prevent unwanted cell killing by restricting caspase activity are poorly understood, but there are strong reasons to explore the role of inhibitory proteins. One important family of caspase inhibitors are the inhibitor of apoptosis proteins (IAPs), which can bind to and inhibit active caspases in both insects and mammals [22,23]. The most compelling evidence for a critical role of IAPs in caspase regulation has come from studies in Drosophila. Drosophila IAP1 (Diap1) encodes an E3 ubiquitin ligase that is strictly required to prevent inappropriate caspase activation and apoptosis [24-27]. In live cells, Diap1 promotes the ubiquitination and degradation of the apoptotic initiator caspase Dronc, and mutations in the RING domain of Diap1 that abrogate E3-ligase activity lead to a dramatic increase of Dronc protein, effector caspase activation, and cell death [28,29]. On the other hand, in cells that are destined to undergo apoptosis, Diap1 is inactivated by Reaper-family (RHG) proteins [24,26,27]. Reaper stimulates the self-conjugation and degradation of Diap1, thereby irreversibly removing this critical caspase inhibitor [30]. Likewise, induction of apoptosis in thymocytes induces the auto-ubiquitination and degradation of mammalian IAPs [31]. These and other observations reveal a critical role of the ubiquitin pathway in the regulation of apoptosis [30,32-37]. Ubiquitin-mediated protein degradation is a tightly regulated process, in which proteins are tagged with ubiquitin moieties through a series of enzymatic reactions involving an E1-activating enzyme, E2-conjugating enzyme, and E3 ubiquitin ligase, which determines substrate specificity. Tagged proteins are then degraded by the 26S proteasome [38-40]. However, thus far no other E3 ligases besides IAPs have been implicated in the direct regulation of caspases.
###end p 8
###begin p 9
###xml 115 125 115 125 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
###xml 474 476 474 476 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b041">41</xref>
###xml 477 479 477 479 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b042">42</xref>
###xml 572 574 572 574 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b041">41</xref>
###xml 575 577 575 577 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b042">42</xref>
###xml 808 810 808 810 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b043">43</xref>
###xml 811 813 811 813 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b048">48</xref>
###xml 1032 1034 1032 1034 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b041">41</xref>
###xml 1035 1037 1035 1037 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b042">42</xref>
###xml 1038 1040 1038 1040 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b049">49</xref>
###xml 1132 1134 1132 1134 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b041">41</xref>
###xml 1286 1294 1286 1294 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cullin-3</italic>
###xml 1414 1424 1414 1424 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
###xml 1669 1671 1669 1671 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b012">12</xref>
###xml 1672 1674 1672 1674 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b050">50</xref>
###xml 2061 2063 2061 2063 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b014">14</xref>
###xml 2064 2066 2064 2066 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b051">51</xref>
###xml 2201 2203 2201 2203 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b014">14</xref>
###xml 2204 2206 2204 2206 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b051">51</xref>
###xml 2207 2209 2207 2209 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b054">54</xref>
###xml 2247 2255 2247 2255 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cullin-3</italic>
###xml 2624 2630 2624 2630 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">klhl10</italic>
###xml 3009 3019 3009 3019 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
###xml 486 491 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
Here we provide evidence that a Cullin-3-based multiprotein complex plays a critical role in caspase activation in Drosophila. Cullins are major components of another type of E3 ubiquitin ligase that serve as scaffolds for two functional modules: a catalytic module, composed of a small RING domain protein that recruits the ubiquitin-conjugating enzyme, and a substrate recognition module that binds to the substrate and brings it within proximity to the catalytic module [41,42]. The human genome encodes seven different Cullins: Cullin-1, -2, -3, -4A, -4B, -5, and -7 [41,42]. The SCF (Skp1-Cullin-1-F-box) complexes are, so far, the best-characterized Cullin-dependent E3 ligases. More recently, the molecular composition and function of the Cullin-3-dependent E3 ligase complex has also been described [43-48]. In this complex, Broad-complex, Tramtrack and Bric-a-Brac (BTB) domain-containing proteins mediate binding of the Cullin to the substrate, whereas the Skp1/F-box heterodimer fulfill this function in the SCF complex [41,42,49]. During the past decade Cullins have been implicated in a variety of cellular activities [41]. However, very little is known about their involvement in the regulation of caspase activation and apoptosis. Here, we describe the identification of cullin-3 mutants from a genetic screen for mutants that abrogate effector caspase activation during terminal differentiation of Drosophila spermatids. In this process, also known as spermatid individualization, spermatids eliminate the majority of their cytoplasm and organelles in an apoptosis-like process that requires canonical cell death proteins, including apoptotic caspases [12,50]. Although caspase activation in this system does not lead to death of the entire cell, sperm individualization resembles apoptosis in the sense that many cellular structures are removed into the "waste bag," which resembles an apoptotic corpse without the nucleus. Another example where apoptotic proteins are used for cellular remodeling is the caspase-dependent pruning of neurites [14,51]. Like in spermatid individualization, the apoptotic machinery is used in a spatially restricted way to destroy only parts of a cell [14,51-54]. In our screen, we isolated several cullin-3 alleles with mutations in a testis-specific N-terminal Cullin-3 (TeNC) domain. We show that the small RING domain protein, Roc1b, interacts with Cullin-3 in spermatids to promote effector caspase activation. We also identified a BTB-domain protein, Klhl10, that selectively binds to the testis-specific form of Cullin-3, but not to somatic Cullin-3. Mutant alleles of klhl10 were isolated that block effector caspase activation and cause male sterility. Finally, the giant IAP-like protein dBruce binds to Klhl10 in S2 cells, suggesting that dBruce may be a substrate for the Cullin-3-dependent ubiquitin ligase complex. Together, these results define a novel Cullin-3-dependent E3 ubiquitin ligase complex that regulates effector caspase activation in Drosophila spermatids. Given the conserved nature of these proteins, our findings may have important implications for caspase regulation in other systems.
###end p 9
###begin title 10
Results
###end title 10
###begin title 11
Mutants Defective in Effector Caspase Activation during Spermatid Individualization
###end title 11
###begin p 12
###xml 28 38 28 38 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
###xml 174 176 174 176 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b055">55</xref>
###xml 484 486 484 486 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b055">55</xref>
###xml 487 489 487 489 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b058">58</xref>
###xml 586 588 586 588 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b012">12</xref>
###xml 589 591 589 591 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b015">15</xref>
###xml 592 594 592 594 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b050">50</xref>
###xml 595 597 595 597 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b059">59</xref>
###xml 760 762 760 762 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b015">15</xref>
###xml 763 765 763 765 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b050">50</xref>
###xml 766 768 766 768 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b060">60</xref>
###xml 769 771 769 771 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b062">62</xref>
###xml 946 948 946 948 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b063">63</xref>
###xml 949 951 949 951 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b064">64</xref>
###xml 1416 1418 1416 1418 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b012">12</xref>
###xml 1419 1421 1419 1421 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b050">50</xref>
During sperm development in Drosophila, a group of 64 post-meiotic spermatids remain initially interconnected by cytoplasmic bridges that result from incomplete cytokinesis [55]. These spermatids are later separated from each other by the caudal movement of an actin-based individualization complex (IC) in a process termed "individualization." During spermatid individualization, the majority of the cytoplasm and cellular organelles are removed and get deposited into "waste bags" [55-58]. This process shares several features with apoptosis and requires apoptotic effector caspases [12,15,50,59]. To gain insight into the regulation of caspases in this system, we screened for mutants that lack staining for an antibody detecting processed caspase-3 (CM1) [15,50,60-62]. We screened a collection of more than 1,000 male-sterile mutant lines defective in spermatid individualization that were previously identified among 12,326 viable mutants [63,64]. Testes from each line were stained with CM1, and 33 CM1-negative alleles representing 22 different complementation groups were identified. However, the vast majority of male-sterile mutants were CM1-positive, even though many displayed severe defects in spermatid individualization. Therefore, consistent with our earlier observations, caspase activation at the onset of spermatid individualization is independent of many other aspects of sperm differentiation [12,50].
###end p 12
###begin p 13
###xml 260 262 260 262 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b065">65</xref>
###xml 263 265 263 265 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b066">66</xref>
###xml 353 362 353 362 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050251-sg001">Figure S1</xref>
###xml 730 736 730 736 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">medusa</italic>
###xml 739 742 739 742 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds</italic>
###xml 804 808 804 808 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds1</italic>
###xml 882 887 882 887 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trans</italic>
###xml 941 949 941 949 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 951 952 951 952 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g001">1</xref>
###xml 958 967 958 967 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050251-sg002">Figure S2</xref>
###xml 989 992 989 992 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds</italic>
###xml 1083 1088 1083 1088 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds1,</italic>
###xml 1180 1199 1180 1199 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila cullin-3</italic>
###xml 1232 1238 1232 1238 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds1&#8211;5</sup>
###xml 1228 1238 1228 1238 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>mds1&#8211;5</sup></italic>
###xml 1252 1287 1252 1287 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Z2&#8211;1089, Z2&#8211;4870, Z2&#8211;4061, Z2&#8211;1270,</italic>
###xml 1292 1299 1292 1299 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Z2&#8211;1062</italic>
###xml 1315 1323 1315 1323 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 1325 1326 1325 1326 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g001">1</xref>
###xml 1334 1338 1334 1338 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds2</sup>
###xml 1330 1338 1330 1338 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>mds2</sup></italic>
###xml 1425 1430 1425 1430 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trans</italic>
To distinguish mutants that specifically affect caspase-3 activation from ones that affect general aspects of spermatid differentiation, we used a monoclonal antibody that detects polyglycylated axonemal tubulin (AXO 49) as an advanced differentiation marker [65,66]. In wild-type spermatids, the pattern of AXO 49 staining is identical to that of CM1 (Figure S1). While mutants in eight of our complementation groups abrogated AXO 49 staining, mutations in the remaining 14 groups retained AXO 49 staining, indicating that these genes act downstream of the general signal(s) required for the initiation of spermatid individualization. One of these complementation groups was represented by five different alleles that we termed "medusa" (mds; in Greek mythology, Medusa represents both life and death). mds1 is AXO 49-positive but completely negative for CM1 as a homozygote or in trans to deficiencies that cover the corresponding region (Figure 1B-1D and Figure S2). The remaining four mds alleles retained various levels of CM1 staining but failed to complement the sterility of mds1, suggesting that they are hypomorphic alleles. All these mutations were later mapped to the Drosophila cullin-3 gene and were thus designed cul3mds1-5 (Zuker lines Z2-1089, Z2-4870, Z2-4061, Z2-1270, and Z2-1062, respectively; Figure 1E-1G). cul3mds2 contains an unrelated lethal mutation in the background and therefore was analyzed in trans to the other alleles or deficiencies in the region.
###end p 13

###xml 619 627 617 625 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>mds1</sup></italic>
###xml 627 630 625 628 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
(I) The diagram depicts a DEVDase activity assay for cul3mds1-/- testes. Caspase-3-like (DEVDase) activity is detected in wild-type testes and is blocked either after treatment with the caspase-3 inhibitor Z-VAD.fmk or in cul3mds1-/- testes. DEVDase activity, presented as relative luminescence units (RLUs), was determined on Ac-DEVD-pNA substrate in testis extracts made of 180 wild-type (yw) or cul3mds1-/- testes treated with Z-VAD or left untreated (DMSO). Readings were obtained every 2 min, and each time interval represents an average (mean +/- SEM) of five readings. Note that the level of DEVDase activity in cul3mds1-/- testes is highly similar to the corresponding level in wild-type testes that were treated with Z-VAD.

###begin p 23
###xml 0 10 0 10 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
###xml 101 103 101 103 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b067">67</xref>
###xml 104 106 104 106 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b069">69</xref>
###xml 229 236 229 236 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cyt-c-d</italic>
###xml 252 254 252 254 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b050">50</xref>
###xml 378 382 378 382 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds1</sup>
###xml 374 382 374 382 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>mds1</sup></italic>
###xml 500 504 500 504 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds1</sup>
###xml 496 504 496 504 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>mds1</sup></italic>
###xml 635 643 635 643 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 649 650 649 650 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g001">1</xref>
###xml 681 689 681 689 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cullin-3</italic>
Drosophila apoptotic effector caspases, such as drICE and Dcp-1, can display DEVD cleaving activity [67-69]. We have previously shown that wild-type adult testes also contain DEVDase activity and that this activity is reduced in cyt-c-d mutant testes [50]. To provide independent evidence for a requirement of Cullin-3 in caspase activation, we measured DEVDase activity in cul3mds1 mutant testes. Whereas lysates of wild-type testes displayed significant levels of DEVDase activity, activity in cul3mds1 mutant testes was reduced to background levels, comparable to the reduction achieved with the potent caspase inhibitor Z-VAD.fmk (Figure 1I and 1J). These results confirm that cullin-3 is required for the activation of effector caspases in spermatids.
###end p 23
###begin title 24
###xml 47 55 47 55 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cullin-3</italic>

###xml 1243 1253 1243 1253 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gft[06430]</sup>
###xml 1239 1254 1239 1254 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>gft[06430]</sup>,</italic>
###xml 1305 1308 1305 1308 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gft</italic>
###xml 1352 1355 1352 1355 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds</italic>
###xml 1453 1461 1453 1461 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cullin-3</italic>
###xml 1463 1471 1463 1471 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 1474 1482 1474 1482 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050251-st001">Table S1</xref>
###xml 1583 1587 1583 1587 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds1</italic>
###xml 1757 1765 1757 1765 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cullin-3</italic>
###xml 1781 1789 1781 1789 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 1795 1796 1795 1796 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g002">2</xref>
###xml 1980 1988 1980 1988 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cullin-3</italic>
###xml 2008 2012 2008 2012 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 2004 2012 2004 2012 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Soma</sub></italic>
###xml 2021 2027 2021 2027 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 2017 2027 2017 2027 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 2029 2037 2029 2037 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 2043 2044 2043 2044 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g002">2</xref>
###xml 2051 2072 2051 2072 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
###xml 2174 2178 2174 2178 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 2170 2178 2170 2178 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Soma</sub></italic>
###xml 2269 2275 2269 2275 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 2265 2275 2265 2275 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 2347 2355 2347 2355 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 2361 2362 2361 2362 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g002">2</xref>
###xml 2507 2511 2507 2511 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 2503 2512 2503 2512 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Soma</sub>,</italic>
###xml 2586 2594 2586 2594 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 2704 2710 2704 2710 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 2700 2710 2700 2710 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
To map the mds alleles, we first searched for genomic deletions that failed to complement the sterility of the mds males. Utilizing the "deficiency kit" from FlyBase, the male-sterility was mapped to genomic segment 35C1-35D1 on the left arm of the second chromosome (Figure S2). We then performed similar complementation tests with available mutants in this region and found that lethal cullin-3 mutants [70,71] failed to complement the sterility of mds mutant males, suggesting that the mds alleles may represent a unique class of mutations in the cullin-3 gene (see below, Table S1). Because the Drosophila cullin-3 gene was previously termed gft [71], we will henceforth refer to the lethal cullin-3 alleles as cul3gft. To determine the molecular nature of the mds mutations, we analyzed first the cullin-3 genomic organization. The cullin-3 gene consists of 14 exons, 11 of which contain coding sequences (Figure 2A; a partial genomic map was provided in [71]). Our genetic and molecular analyses identified a new exon, 1D, and suggested that the cullin-3 gene codes for two major isoforms that are somatic and testis specific (Figure 2A and 2B). A lethal P-element insertion in the 5' untranslated region (UTR) of the cullin-3 gene, cul3gft[06430], which failed to complement the lethality of other gft alleles, complemented the sterility of the mds alleles, suggesting that these noncoding sequences are only required for the somatic function of cullin-3 (Figure 2A, Table S1, and unpublished data). Additionally, genomic PCR followed by sequencing analysis revealed that the mds1 mutant contains a deletion in the intron that is flanked by exon 2 and exon 3, suggesting that this intron contains sequences that are only required for the function of cullin-3 in spermatids (Figure 2A and 2C). Finally, reverse-transcriptase (RT)-PCR as well as sequence analyses of several independent clones from adult testis and somatic cDNA libraries confirmed the presence of two major cullin-3 mRNA isoforms, cul3Soma and cul3Testis (Figure 2A and 2B; see Materials and Methods for details about the cDNA clones). While both isoforms share extensive similarity (exons 3-11), cul3Soma contains a unique, 20-amino-acid-long N-terminal polypeptide (encoded by exon 2), and cul3Testis contains a unique, 181-amino-acid-long TeNC domain encoded by exon 1D (Figure 2A and 2B; part of exon 1D is incorrectly annotated in FlyBase as an independent gene, CG31829). We also identified three different mRNA isoforms of cul3Soma, but these only differ in their 5' UTRs (encoded by exons 1A, 1B, and 1C, Figure 2A). Cullins were previously thought to be universally expressed. Therefore, to the best of our knowledge, cul3Testis represents the first tissue-specific Cullin identified in any organism.
###end p 25
###begin title 26
###xml 8 14 8 14 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds1&#8211;5</sup>
###xml 4 14 4 14 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>mds1&#8211;5</sup></italic>
###xml 62 70 62 70 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cullin-3</italic>
The cul3mds1-5 Alleles Contain Mutations in a New Exon of the cullin-3 Gene

###begin p 27
###xml 32 40 32 40 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cullin-3</italic>

###xml 841 854 841 854 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gft2, 4, GR18</sup>

###xml 965 971 965 971 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds1&#8211;5</sup>
###xml 961 971 961 971 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>mds1&#8211;5</sup></italic>

###xml 1015 1022 1015 1022 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>gft</sup></italic>
###xml 1049 1051 1049 1051 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b071">71</xref>
###xml 1058 1066 1058 1066 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gft06430</sup>
###xml 1054 1066 1054 1066 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>gft06430</sup></italic>
###xml 1078 1080 1078 1080 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PZ</italic>
###xml 1182 1191 1182 1191 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gft[GR18]</sup>
###xml 1178 1191 1178 1191 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>gft[GR18]</sup></italic>
###xml 1277 1281 1277 1281 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gft4</sup>
###xml 1273 1281 1273 1281 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>gft4</sup></italic>
###xml 1357 1361 1357 1361 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gft2</sup>
###xml 1353 1361 1353 1361 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>gft2</sup></italic>
(A) Genomic organization of the cullin-3 locus. Thick bars indicate exons and dotted lines indicate introns. Solid bars indicate coding sequences, whereas open bars indicate UTRs. The Drosophila cullin-3 gene contains 14 exons, nine of which encode the bulk of the protein (exons 3-11) and are shared by both the somatic and testis-specific isoforms. While the three somatic isoforms (cul3Soma) differ in their 5' UTRs, each beginning with a unique first exon (exons 1A, 1B, and 1C), they share a second, somatic-only exon that contains a start codon (exon 2, green bar). The testis isoform, cul3Testis, begins with a unique first exon (1D, blue bar) that includes both 5' UTR and coding sequences, including a start codon. The relative locations of the molecular lesions in cul3Testis (orange, cul3mds1-5 alleles) and cul3Soma (purple, cul3gft2, 4, GR18 alleles) are shown with stars (see the main text for more details on the precise molecular lesions of the cul3mds1-5 alleles). The molecular alterations of the cul3gft alleles were reported in [71]: cul3gft06430 contains a PZ element insertion 228 nucleotides from exon 2 (the insertion is indicated by a purple triangle). cul3gft[GR18] is missing a single nucleotide causing a premature stop codon at amino acid 167. cul3gft4 bears a C-to-T transversion, which results in an A710-to-V conversion. cul3gft2 contains a five-nucleotide deletion that results in a premature stop codon at amino acid 748 that removes half of the C-terminal Cullin homology domain (CHD).

###xml 964 970 964 970 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 960 970 960 970 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 972 980 972 980 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 1017 1020 1017 1020 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gft</italic>
###xml 1075 1078 1075 1078 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1072 1078 1072 1078 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1089 1098 1089 1098 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gft[GR18]</sup>
###xml 1085 1098 1085 1098 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>gft[GR18]</sup></italic>
###xml 1104 1108 1104 1108 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gft4</sup>
###xml 1100 1108 1100 1108 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>gft4</sup></italic>
###xml 1118 1122 1118 1122 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gft2</sup>
###xml 1114 1122 1114 1122 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>gft2</sup></italic>
###xml 1215 1223 1215 1223 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cullin-3</italic>
###xml 1241 1249 1241 1249 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 1253 1255 1253 1255 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b071">71</xref>
To determine the molecular nature of the mds alleles, we sequenced PCR-amplified genomic fragments of the cullin-3 locus from these mutants. As expected from the genetic analysis, all mds alleles contained mutations in or near exon 1D and hence affect only the testis-specific isoform: cul3mds1 has a 181-bp deletion that eliminates part of 5' UTR of cul3Testis (orange brackets in Figure 2A and 2C). The two hypomorphic alleles, cul3mds3 and cul3mds4, contain a C-to-T transversion at positions 341 and 347, which convert glutamine to stop codons at amino acids 8 and 10, respectively. As a result, translation may initiate downstream of the normal translation initiation site (orange stars in Figure 2A and Figure S3). cul3mds2 contains a G-to-A transversion of a splice donor site in the intron that is flanked by exons 1D and 3; this presumably abrogates splicing between these exons (Figure 2A). cul3mds5 has a G114-to-A transversion within the 5' UTR of cul3Testis (Figure 2A). In contrast, three of the lethal gft alleles that failed to complement the sterility of mds-/- males-cul3gft[GR18], cul3gft4, and cul3gft2-contain mutations in exons 4, 10, and 11, respectively, that are shared by both isoforms of cullin-3 (purple stars in Figure 1A; [71]).
###end p 36
###begin p 37
###xml 43 47 43 47 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds1</sup>
###xml 39 47 39 47 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>mds1</sup></italic>
###xml 64 67 64 67 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gft</italic>
###xml 80 84 80 84 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gft2</sup>
###xml 76 84 76 84 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>gft2</sup></italic>
###xml 90 99 90 99 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gft[GR18]</sup>
###xml 86 99 86 99 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>gft[GR18]</sup></italic>
###xml 105 109 105 109 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gft1</sup>
###xml 101 109 101 109 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>gft1</sup></italic>
###xml 119 128 119 128 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gft[d577]</sup>
###xml 115 128 115 128 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>gft[d577]</sup></italic>
###xml 213 221 213 221 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 224 225 224 225 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g002">2</xref>
###xml 228 229 228 229 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g002">2</xref>
###xml 232 240 232 240 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050251-st001">Table S1</xref>
###xml 271 278 271 278 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds/gft</italic>
###xml 446 455 446 455 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g001">Figures 1</xref>
###xml 458 459 458 459 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g002">2</xref>
###xml 462 470 462 470 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050251-st001">Table S1</xref>
###xml 472 481 472 481 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050251-sg004">Figure S4</xref>
###xml 576 584 576 584 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cullin-3</italic>
Transheterozygous combinations between cul3mds1 and four strong gft alleles-cul3gft2, cul3gft[GR18], cul3gft1, and cul3gft[d577]-were sterile, and their elongated spermatids were CM1-negative but AXO 49-positive (Figure 2E, 2G, 2H, Table S1, and unpublished data). Other mds/gft combinations with weaker alleles produced reduced levels of cleaved caspase-3 staining, wild-type levels of axonemal tubulin polyglycylation, and decreased fertility (Figures 1H, 2I, Table S1, Figure S4, and unpublished data). Collectively, these results suggest that a testis-specific isoform of cullin-3 is required for effector caspase activation and spermatid individualization.
###end p 37

###xml 18 24 18 24 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 14 24 14 24 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
Expression of cul3Testis Is Restricted to the Male Germline

###begin p 39
###xml 100 106 100 106 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>

###xml 502 510 502 510 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Soma</sub></italic>
###xml 601 607 601 607 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 597 607 597 607 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 641 649 641 649 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 798 804 798 804 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 794 804 794 804 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 920 928 920 928 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cullin-3</italic>
###xml 971 975 971 975 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 967 975 967 975 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Soma</sub></italic>
###xml 1064 1067 1064 1067 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1059 1067 1059 1067 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">oskar<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1077 1085 1077 1085 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 1099 1105 1099 1105 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 1095 1105 1095 1105 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 1166 1172 1166 1172 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 1162 1172 1162 1172 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 1231 1235 1231 1235 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 1227 1235 1227 1235 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Soma</sub></italic>
###xml 1307 1315 1307 1315 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 1321 1322 1321 1322 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g003">3</xref>
###xml 1402 1407 1402 1407 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testi</sub>
###xml 1398 1407 1398 1407 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testi</sub></italic>
###xml 1407 1408 1407 1408 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">s</sub>
###xml 1427 1431 1427 1431 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds1</sup>
###xml 1423 1431 1423 1431 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>mds1</sup></italic>
###xml 1441 1449 1441 1449 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 1465 1471 1465 1471 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 1461 1471 1461 1471 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 1517 1524 1517 1524 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds1&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1513 1524 1513 1524 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>mds1&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 1548 1552 1548 1552 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds1</sup>
###xml 1544 1552 1544 1552 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>mds1</sup></italic>
###xml 1608 1614 1608 1614 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 1604 1614 1604 1614 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 1628 1636 1628 1636 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 1642 1643 1642 1643 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g003">3</xref>
###xml 1705 1711 1705 1711 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 1701 1711 1701 1711 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 1741 1745 1741 1745 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 1737 1745 1737 1745 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Soma</sub></italic>
###xml 1864 1872 1864 1872 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cullin-3</italic>
Our genetic analyses suggested the existence of two functionally distinct isoforms of cullin-3, cul3Testis, and cul3Soma. One possible explanation for this is that the two isoforms are differentially expressed. To test this idea, we examined the distribution of cullin-3 transcripts in the testis and the soma. Comparative RT-PCR experiments were performed using specific primers in the unique 5' UTRs of cul3Soma and cul3Testis and a reverse primer in their common 3' UTR (black arrows in Figure 3A). cul3Soma was the only isoform detectable in the soma of adult females (which lack testes), and cul3Testis was the major isoform in testes (Figure 3B). Dissected testes contain both germ cells and somatic cells, such as the testicular wall, muscles cells, and cyst cells. To determine whether cul3Testis is germ-cell specific, we also analyzed RNA from a mutant lacking germ cells. Both the somatic and testis forms of cullin-3 were expressed in wild type, but only cul3Soma was detected in the germ-cell-less reproductive tracts of adult males derived from oskar-/- mothers (Figure 3C). Since cul3Testis is not detectable in adult females, this indicates that cul3Testis expression is restricted to male germ cells, and that cul3Soma expression is mainly, if not exclusively, restricted to somatic cells (Figure 3B and 3C). Finally, consistent with the idea that promoter and 5' UTR sequences of cul3Testis are absent in cul3mds1 mutants (Figure 2A), neither cul3Testis transcripts nor protein were detected in cul3mds1-/- testes. Therefore, cul3mds1 has both the genetic and molecular properties of a cul3Testis null allele (Figure 3B and 3D). These results suggest that differential expression of cul3Testis in the male germline and cul3Soma in somatic tissues accounts for the distinct phenotypes (male sterility versus lethality) of the different classes of cullin-3 mutations.
###end p 39

###xml 22 28 22 28 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 18 28 18 28 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
The Expression of cul3Testis Is Restricted to Male Germ Cells

###xml 32 51 32 51 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila cullin-3</italic>
###xml 72 78 72 78 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 68 78 68 78 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>

###begin p 42
###xml 20 26 20 26 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 16 26 16 26 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 38 42 38 42 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 34 42 34 42 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Soma</sub></italic>
###xml 147 153 147 153 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 143 153 143 153 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 172 176 172 176 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 168 176 168 176 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Soma</sub></italic>
###xml 504 510 504 510 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 500 510 500 510 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 593 597 593 597 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 589 597 589 597 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Soma</sub></italic>
###xml 627 631 627 631 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 623 631 623 631 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Soma</sub></italic>
###xml 743 749 743 749 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 739 749 739 749 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 783 787 783 787 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds1</sup>
###xml 779 787 779 787 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>mds1</sup></italic>
###xml 838 844 838 844 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 834 844 834 844 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
(B) Analysis of cul3Testis versus cul3Soma expression in the testis and the soma. The above primers (arrows in A) to amplify either a 2,997-bp cul3Testis or a 2,642-bp cul3Soma cDNA fragment were added to one reaction master-mix. The reaction was stopped at different cycle points to identify the linear amplification phase (30 and 35 cycles are indicated). The "RT" columns represent reverse transcriptase followed by PCR reactions, and the "Taq" are the control, PCR-only, reactions. Note that the cul3Testis expression levels were much higher in the wild-type (WT) testes than these of cul3Soma. On the other hand, only cul3Soma transcripts were detected in somatic tissues, which are represented by adult female flies. In addition, no cul3Testis transcripts were detected in cul3mds1 mutant testes, confirming that this is a null cul3Testis allele.
###end p 42

###begin title 45
###xml 23 29 23 29 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
The TeNC Domain in Cul3Testis Is Required for Caspase Activation and Male Fertility
###end title 45
###begin p 46
###xml 107 109 107 109 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b041">41</xref>
###xml 110 112 110 112 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b042">42</xref>
###xml 115 123 115 123 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g009">Figure 9</xref>
###xml 201 207 201 207 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 245 249 245 249 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 334 340 334 340 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 461 467 461 467 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 457 467 457 467 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 475 479 475 479 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 471 479 471 479 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Soma</sub></italic>
###xml 509 515 509 515 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 505 515 505 515 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 545 553 545 553 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 565 586 565 586 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
###xml 682 686 682 686 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds1</sup>
###xml 678 686 678 686 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>mds1</sup></italic>
###xml 768 777 768 777 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g004">Figures 4</xref>
###xml 783 784 783 784 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g004">4</xref>
###xml 916 920 916 920 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds1</sup>
###xml 912 920 912 920 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>mds1</sup></italic>
###xml 993 999 993 999 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 989 999 989 999 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 1102 1110 1102 1110 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 1116 1117 1116 1117 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g004">4</xref>
###xml 1247 1251 1247 1251 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds1</sup>
###xml 1243 1251 1243 1251 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>mds1</sup></italic>
###xml 1288 1296 1288 1296 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cullin-3</italic>
###xml 1341 1345 1341 1345 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 1337 1345 1337 1345 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Soma</sub></italic>
###xml 1393 1399 1393 1399 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 1389 1399 1389 1399 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 1435 1439 1435 1439 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 1431 1439 1431 1439 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Soma</sub></italic>
###xml 1549 1557 1549 1557 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 1563 1564 1563 1564 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g004">4</xref>
###xml 1582 1586 1582 1586 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 1578 1586 1578 1586 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Soma</sub></italic>
###xml 1595 1601 1595 1601 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 1591 1601 1591 1601 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
The N-terminal region of Cullins is thought to mediate binding to a specific substrate recognition module [41,42] (Figure 9). To test whether the unique TeNC domain is required for the function of Cul3Testis, we tested whether expression of Cul3Soma, which lacks a TeNC domain, was able to functionally substitute for the loss of Cul3Testis in developing spermatids. For this purpose, we generated transgenic flies that express the coding regions of either cul3Testis or cul3Soma under the control of the cul3Testis promoter and 5' and 3' UTRs (Figure 4A; see also Materials and Methods). At least three independent transgenic lines for each of these constructs were crossed to cul3mds1 flies, and proper expression of the transgenes was confirmed by RT-PCR analysis (Figures 4B and 4C). We examined the ability of these transgenes to rescue caspase activation, spermatid individualization and male sterility of cul3mds1 flies. As expected, transgenes with either one or two copies of the cul3Testis open reading frame (ORF) fully rescued CM1-staining, spermatid individualization, and male fertility (Figure 4E and 4F; note the reappearance of cystic bulges and waste bags). This proves that both the caspase and sterility phenotypes seen in cul3mds1 mutant flies are due to the loss of cullin-3 function. We next tested the ability of cul3Soma to functionally substitute for the loss of cul3Testis. Neither one nor two copies of cul3Soma rescued spermatid individualization or male fertility, although we observed very low levels of CM1-staining (Figure 4H and 4I). Since the cul3Soma and cul3Testis ORF transgenes were expressed under the same promoter and at comparable levels, we conclude that the TeNC domain is necessary for efficient caspase activation and spermatid individualization.
###end p 46
###begin title 47
###xml 4 10 4 10 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 0 10 0 10 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 23 27 23 27 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 19 27 19 27 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Soma</sub></italic>
###xml 98 104 98 104 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 94 104 94 104 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
