###begin title 57
###xml 0 5 0 5 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">roc1b</italic>
###xml 37 43 37 43 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 33 43 33 43 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
roc1b Genetically Interacts with cul3Testis To Facilitate Effector Caspase Activation
###end title 57
###begin p 58
###xml 192 194 192 194 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b042">42</xref>
###xml 195 197 195 197 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b049">49</xref>
###xml 198 200 198 200 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b072">72</xref>
###xml 207 217 207 217 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
###xml 363 365 363 365 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b073">73</xref>
###xml 436 441 436 441 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">roc1b</italic>
###xml 491 493 491 493 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b073">73</xref>
###xml 494 496 494 496 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b074">74</xref>
###xml 616 618 616 618 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b074">74</xref>
###xml 659 664 659 664 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">roc1b</italic>
###xml 757 763 757 763 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dc3&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 752 763 752 763 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">roc1b<sup>dc3&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 845 853 845 853 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g005">Figure 5</xref>
###xml 873 878 873 878 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">roc1b</italic>
###xml 910 916 910 916 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 906 917 906 917 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub>,</italic>
###xml 959 962 959 962 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dc3</sup>
###xml 954 962 954 962 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">roc1b<sup>dc3</sup></italic>
###xml 987 990 987 990 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds</sup>
###xml 983 990 983 990 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>mds</sup></italic>
###xml 1034 1037 1034 1037 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds</sup>
###xml 1030 1037 1030 1037 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>mds</sup></italic>
###xml 1046 1049 1046 1049 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dc3</sup>
###xml 1041 1049 1041 1049 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">roc1b<sup>dc3</sup></italic>
###xml 1090 1098 1090 1098 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 1100 1101 1100 1101 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g001">1</xref>
###xml 1107 1115 1107 1115 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g005">Figure 5</xref>
###xml 1230 1236 1230 1236 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 1226 1236 1226 1236 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 1264 1269 1264 1269 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">roc1b</italic>
###xml 1315 1323 1315 1323 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g005">Figure 5</xref>
Cullins contain a C-terminal cullin homology domain (CHD) that can bind small RING domain proteins, which in turn recruit a ubiquitin-conjugating enzyme (E2) to generate the catalytic module [42,49,72]. The Drosophila genome contains three small RING domain proteins, Roc1a, Roc1b, and Roc2, all of which are capable of activating ubiquitin conjugation in vitro [73]. Loss of Roc1a function causes lethality, and targeted disruption of roc1b was previously reported to cause male sterility [73,74]. Furthermore, Cullin-3 preferentially co-immunoprecipitates with Roc1b, indicating that both proteins form a complex [74]. We therefore examined whether loss of roc1b function affects caspase activation and individualization of spermatids. We found that roc1bdc3-/- spermatids displayed reduced levels of CM1 staining and failed to individualize (Figure 5A). To test whether roc1b genetically interacts with cul3Testis, we generated double mutants between roc1bdc3 and the hypomorphic cul3mds alleles. Homozygous mutants for either cul3mds or roc1bdc3 showed moderate levels of CM1 staining (Figure 1E-1G and Figure 5B). In contrast, CM1 staining was completely abolished in spermatids of the double mutants, demonstrating that cul3Testis genetically interacts with roc1b to promote caspase activation in spermatids (Figure 5C). These results support the idea that Roc1b is a functionally relevant partner of Cullin-3 in vivo.
###end p 58
###begin title 59
###xml 23 29 23 29 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 19 29 19 29 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 34 39 34 39 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">roc1b</italic>
Double Mutants for cul3Testis and roc1b Block Caspase Activation During Spermatid Differentiation
###end title 59
###begin p 60
###xml 108 113 108 113 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">roc1b</italic>

###xml 128 136 128 136 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">roc1b<sup>dc3</sup></italic>
###xml 136 139 136 139 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 288 294 288 294 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 284 294 284 294 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>

###begin title 61
###xml 4 10 4 10 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 74 79 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">Yeast</span>
Cul3Testis Preferentially Interacts with the BTB Domain Protein Klhl10 in Yeast
###end title 61
###begin p 62
###xml 92 94 92 94 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b044">44</xref>
###xml 95 97 95 97 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b045">45</xref>
###xml 98 100 98 100 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b049">49</xref>
###xml 216 226 216 226 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
###xml 228 230 228 230 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b042">42</xref>
###xml 231 233 231 233 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b049">49</xref>
###xml 312 318 312 318 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 374 380 374 380 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 403 413 403 413 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
###xml 421 429 421 429 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g006">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 440 461 440 461 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
###xml 502 512 502 512 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
###xml 647 655 647 655 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g006">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 721 731 721 731 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
###xml 770 780 770 780 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
###xml 835 837 835 837 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b044">44</xref>
###xml 838 840 838 840 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b075">75</xref>
###xml 841 843 841 843 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b078">78</xref>
###xml 908 914 908 914 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 1088 1094 1088 1094 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 1100 1104 1100 1104 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 1211 1217 1211 1217 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 1225 1229 1225 1229 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 1258 1264 1258 1264 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 1271 1279 1271 1279 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g006">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 1285 1286 1285 1286 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g006">6</xref>
###xml 1551 1557 1551 1557 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 251 256 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 672 677 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 748 753 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1148 1153 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
Cullin-3-dependent E3 ligases use BTB domain containing proteins for substrate recognition [44,45,49]. The number of genes encoding BTB domain containing proteins is very large, with an estimated 140-250 proteins in Drosophila [42,49]. We performed a yeast two hybrid (Y2H) screen using the coding region of Cul3Testis as bait to identify potential protein partners for Cul3Testis in a library of adult Drosophila cDNAs (Figure 6; see also Materials and Methods). Several cDNA clones, which encode for Drosophila orthologues of three BTB domain-containing proteins, Spop (CG9924), Ipp (CG9426), and Klhl10 (CG12423), were isolated in this screen (Figure 6). Notably, both mouse Klhl10, which shares 46% identity with its Drosophila counterpart and mouse Spop as well as Drosophila Spop were previously shown to interact with Cullin-3 [44,75-78]. Given our previous results implicating the TeNC domain in Cul3Testis function, we asked whether any of these proteins bind preferentially to this domain. For this, we examined interactions between these BTB domain-containing proteins and Cul3Testis, Cul3Soma, or the TeNC domain alone in two different yeast strains. Whereas Spop and Ipp interacted with either Cul3Testis or Cul3Soma, Klhl10 interacted with Cul3Testis only (Figure 6A and 6B). However, the TeNC domain alone was not able to bind to any of the BTB domain-containing proteins in this assay. We conclude that the TeNC domain is required but not sufficient for BTB protein binding. These results identify Klhl10 as a potential partner of Cul3Testis in spermatids.
###end p 62
###begin title 63
###xml 75 81 75 81 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 99 103 99 103 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
Klhl10, a BTB and Kelch Domains Protein, Preferentially Interacts with Cul3Testis and Not with Cul3Soma
###end title 63
###begin p 64
###xml 35 45 35 45 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 116 122 116 122 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 251 255 248 252 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 288 294 285 291 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 325 331 322 328 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 128 133 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
(A) Three BTB-domain proteins, the Drosophila orthologues of Spop, Ipp, and Klhl10, were found to interact with Cul3Testis in a yeast-two-hybrid screen. beta-galactosidase filter assay demonstrates that whereas Spop and Ipp can also interact with Cul3Soma, Klhl10 only interacts with Cul3Testis. While the TeNC domain of Cul3Testis is required for this interaction, it is not sufficient to mediate the interaction with Klhl10.
###end p 64
###begin p 65
###xml 72 78 72 78 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 251 255 251 255 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 533 537 533 537 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 51 57 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeasts</span>
###xml 225 230 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
(B) Similarly, in a nutrient-omitted medium assay, yeasts with both Cul3Testis and Klhl10 grew rapidly (2 d) on plates that lacked, in addition to leucine and tryptophan (-2), also histidine and adenine (-4 plates). However, yeast with Klhl10 and Cul3Soma grew very poorly on -4 plates. Even after two weeks of incubation, the colony is only partially established. Note that the results for the auxotrophy rescue of Klhl10 are shown not after 2 d but rather after 14 d in order to reflect the weak interaction between Klhl10 and Cul3Soma.
###end p 65
###begin p 66
(C) Schematic representations of Spop, Ipp, and Klhl10, and the relative locations of their major domains. The BTB-domains of all these proteins are sufficient for binding to Cullin-3.
###end p 66
###begin title 67
###xml 13 19 13 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">klhl10</italic>
Mutations in klhl10 Abrogate Effector Caspase Activation during Spermatid Individualization
###end title 67
###begin p 68
###xml 94 100 94 100 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">klhl10</italic>
###xml 288 294 288 294 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">klhl10</italic>
###xml 459 465 459 465 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">klhl10</italic>
###xml 481 484 481 484 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1&#8211;7</sup>
###xml 474 485 474 485 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">(klhl10<sup>1&#8211;7</sup>)</italic>
###xml 697 705 697 705 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g007">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 707 708 707 708 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g007">7</xref>
###xml 790 796 790 796 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 886 892 886 892 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">klhl10</italic>
###xml 902 910 902 910 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g007">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 916 917 916 917 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g007">7</xref>
###xml 950 953 950 953 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2&#8211;6</sup>
###xml 944 953 944 953 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">klhl10<sup>2&#8211;6</sup></italic>
###xml 967 1002 967 1002 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Z2&#8211;1331, Z2&#8211;0960, Z2&#8211;2739, Z2&#8211;3284,</italic>
###xml 1007 1014 1007 1014 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Z2&#8211;4385</italic>
###xml 1181 1189 1181 1189 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g007">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 1195 1196 1195 1196 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g007">7</xref>
###xml 1292 1300 1292 1300 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g007">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 1327 1328 1327 1328 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">7</sup>
###xml 1321 1338 1321 1338 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">klhl10<sup>7</sup> (Z2&#8211;3353)</italic>
###xml 1466 1474 1466 1474 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g007">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 1527 1528 1527 1528 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1</sup>
###xml 1521 1539 1521 1539 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">klhl10<sup>1</sup> (Z2&#8211;1827),</italic>
###xml 1755 1761 1755 1761 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">klhl10</italic>
###xml 1805 1811 1805 1811 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 1801 1811 1801 1811 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 1840 1846 1840 1846 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 1836 1846 1836 1846 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 1867 1888 1867 1888 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
###xml 1980 1986 1980 1986 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">klhl10</italic>
###xml 2003 2012 2003 2012 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g007">Figures 7</xref>
###xml 2018 2019 2018 2019 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g007">7</xref>
###xml 2068 2074 2068 2074 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 2200 2210 2200 2210 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
If Klhl10 is indeed a physiologically relevant Cullin-3 binding partner in vivo, mutations in klhl10 should affect the function of this E3 complex and thus block caspase activation. To test this hypothesis, we searched for loss-of-function mutations in this gene. Genetic analysis of the klhl10 gene is complicated because of its position within a heterochromatic, cytologically unmapped portion on the 2nd chromosome. However, we were able to identify seven klhl10 alleles (klhl101-7) in our collection of CM1-defective mutants. All alleles were defective in spermatid individualization, were recessive male-sterile, failed to complement each other, lacked CM1 staining but were AXO 49-positive (Figure 7A-7F and unpublished data). This phenotype is virtually identical to the loss of Cul3Testis function. By using RT-PCR and sequence analyses, we identified mutations in six of these klhl10 alleles (Figure 7I and 7J). Five of these alleles, klhl102-6 (Zuker lines Z2-1331, Z2-0960, Z2-2739, Z2-3284, and Z2-4385) have mutations in highly conserved amino acids of the Kelch repeats, a domain that mediates interaction with the substrate (colored stars and amino acid residues in Figure 7I and 7J, respectively; more details on the molecular nature of these mutations are in the legends for Figure 7). A sixth mutation, klhl107 (Z2-3353) contains a G508-to-A transversion that converts a highly conserved alanine (A170) to threonine in the BTB domain (gray star in Figure 7I). No mutations were identified in the ORF of klhl101 (Z2-1827), suggesting that this allele carries a mutation in a regulatory region. To prove that these mutations are indeed responsible for the observed phenotypes, we conducted transgenic rescue experiments. Expression of the klhl10 coding region under the control of the cul3Testis promoter (together with cul3Testis 5' and 3' UTRs, see Materials and Methods) completely restored CM1 staining and rescued all the sterility phenotypes associated with klhl10 mutant alleles (Figures 7G and 7H). Collectively, these results suggest that Cul3Testis interacts functionally and physically with Roc1b and Klhl10 to promote caspase activation and spermatid individualization in Drosophila.
###end p 68

###xml 775 782 775 782 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">klhl10<sup>5</sup></italic>

###xml 888 895 888 895 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">klhl10<sup>6</sup></italic>
###xml 897 904 897 904 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Z2&#8211;4385</italic>
###xml 1031 1032 1031 1032 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">7</sup>
###xml 1025 1032 1025 1032 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">klhl10<sup>7</sup></italic>
###xml 1034 1041 1034 1041 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Z2&#8211;3353</italic>
(I) Schematic representation of the Klhl10 protein. The relative locations of the BTB, BACK, and Kelch domains are depicted by thick bars. Different colored stars depict the locations of the different mutations, and the colors correspond to the colored amino-acids in (J). The molecular nature of the mutations and their color code are as follows: klhl102 (Z2-1331) carries a G1801-to-A transversion that converts glutamic acid (E601, red) to lysine at repeat VI. klhl103 (Z2-0960) carries a G1119-to-A transversion that converts tryptophan (W373, purple) to stop codon, resulting in a deletion of most of the Kelch domain. klhl104 (Z2-2739) carries a C1237-to-T transversion that converts arginine (R413, yellow) to stop codon, which also deletes most of the Kelch repeats. klhl105 (Z2-3284) carries a G1486-to-A transversion that converts glycine (G496, blue) to arginine at repeat IV. klhl106 (Z2-4385) carries a C1439-to-T transversion that converts serine (S480, green) to phenylalanine at repeat IV. On the other hand, klhl107 (Z2-3353) carries a G508-to-A transversion that converts a highly conserved alanine (A170) to threonine in the BTB domain (gray star).

###xml 147 148 144 145 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">-</italic>

(J) Alignment of the six Kelch repeats of Klhl10. The alignment is based on the crystal structure of the Keap1 Kelch domain which folds into a beta-propeller structure with 6 blades. The residue range for each blade is indicated at the left. The four conserved beta-strands in each blade are indicated above the sequences by arrows. Residues conserved in all six blades are highlighted with dark gray and appear in upper case in the consensus line, whereas residues that are conserved in at least three blades appear in lower case. Any two and above conserved residues are highlighted with light gray. Color highlighted residues are mutated in the various klhl10-/- alleles and correspond to the stars in (I).

###begin title 76
Elevated Level of Ubiquitinated Protein Expression in Individualizing Spermatids Requires an Intact Cul3-Roc1b-Klhl10 Complex
###end title 76
###begin p 77
###xml 309 315 309 315 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 700 708 700 708 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g008">Figure 8</xref>
###xml 931 939 931 939 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g008">Figure 8</xref>
###xml 1091 1099 1091 1099 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g008">Figure 8</xref>
###xml 1101 1102 1101 1102 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g008">8</xref>
###xml 1220 1228 1220 1228 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g008">Figure 8</xref>
###xml 1358 1366 1358 1366 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g008">Figure 8</xref>
###xml 1368 1369 1368 1369 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g008">8</xref>
###xml 1374 1383 1374 1383 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050251-sg001">Figure S1</xref>
###xml 1389 1391 1389 1391 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050251-sg001">S1</xref>
###xml 1399 1407 1399 1407 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 1412 1414 1412 1414 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b012">12</xref>
###xml 1676 1682 1676 1682 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 1672 1682 1672 1682 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 1687 1693 1687 1693 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">klhl10</italic>
###xml 1849 1857 1849 1857 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g008">Figure 8</xref>
###xml 1863 1864 1863 1864 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g008">8</xref>
###xml 2052 2058 2052 2058 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 2058 2061 2058 2061 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 2048 2061 2048 2061 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub><sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 2072 2075 2072 2075 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 2066 2075 2066 2075 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">klhl10<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 2083 2091 2083 2091 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g008">Figure 8</xref>
###xml 2093 2094 2093 2094 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g008">8</xref>
Our results suggest that a Cul3-Roc1b-Klhl10 E3 ubiquitin ligase complex functions at the onset of spermatid individualization. To explore this further, we investigated the level and spatiotemporal distribution of ubiquitinated proteins during spermatid individualization, and the consequences of loss of Cul3Testis and Klhl10 function on this pattern. For this purpose, we stained wild-type testes with the FK2 monoclonal antibody, which specifically detects ubiquitin-conjugated proteins but not free ubiquitin. At the onset of individualization, a steep gradient of ubiquitinated protein expression is detected from the nuclear heads of the spermatids to the tips of their tails (yellow arrows in Figure 8A). During the caudal translocation of the IC, ubiquitinated proteins became completely depleted from the newly individualized portion of the spermatids (the region that is flanked by a white arrowhead and a white arrow in Figure 8A). The staining remained abundant, however, in the pre-individualized portion of the spermatids, with the highest levels seen in the cystic bulge (CB; Figure 8A-8C). At the end of individualization, the newly formed waste bag (WB) contained high levels of ubiquitinated proteins (Figure 8D). This spatiotemporal pattern of protein ubiquitination is very similar to the distribution of active effector caspase (compare Figure 8A-8D to Figure S1B and S1E or to Figure 2 in [12]). This striking correlation supports the idea that protein ubiquitination facilitates effector caspase activation in individualizing spermatids. Next, to test whether the observed ubiquitination process depends on an intact Cul3-Klhl10 complex, we stained cul3Testis and klhl10 mutant spermatids with the FK2 antibody. The overall level of protein ubiquitination was dramatically decreased in elongated spermatids from both mutants (Figure 8E and 8F). Furthermore, this reduction was specific to late elongated spermatids, because protein ubiquitination during early stages of spermatid maturation was not significantly affected in cul3Testis-/- and klhl10-/- flies (Figure 8G-8I). These results show that protein ubiquitination during spermatid individualization is largely mediated by the Cul3-Klhl10 complex. Therefore, we conclude that the Cul3-Roc1b-Klhl10 complex is functionally active as an E3 ubiquitin ligase to promote protein ubiquitination during spermatid individualization.
###end p 77
###begin title 78
The Cul3-Roc1b-Klhl10 Complex Promotes Protein Ubiquitination during Spermatid Individualization
###end title 78
###begin p 79
Testes were stained with the anti-multi-ubiquitin monoclonal antibody (FK2) that detects ubiquitinated proteins (green), phalloidin, which marks the individualization complex (IC, red), and DAPI to visualize the nuclei (blue).
###end p 79
###begin p 80
(A) Before the formation of an IC, very low levels of ubiquitinated proteins are detected (yellow arrowhead). Once a mature IC is assembled in the vicinity of the nuclei, a steep gradient of ubiquitinated protein staining is detected from the very bottom of the nuclei to the tip of the spermatids' tails (yellow arrows). After the caudal translocation of the IC, ubiquitinated proteins are no longer detectable in the post-individualized portion of the spermatids (the region between the nuclei, indicated by a white arrowhead, and an early CB, indicated by a white arrow).
###end p 80
###begin p 81
(B and C) When the bulk cytoplasm of the spermatids accumulates in a cystic bulge (CB), ubiquitinated proteins are prominent within the CB and the pre-individualized region (white asterisks).
###end p 81
###begin p 82
(D) Once all the cytoplasm is stripped away, ubiquitinated proteins are detectable only in the waste bag (WB).
###end p 82
###begin p 83

(G) Protein ubiquitination is detected in nuclei of early elongating spermatids.

###begin title 87
Working Model for a Cullin-3-Based Ubiquitin Ligase Complex in the Testis
###end title 87
###begin p 88
The diagram represents the assembly of the testis-specific Cullin-3-containing ubiquitin ligase (E3) and its proposed function in caspase activation during spermatid individualization.
###end p 88
###begin p 89
###xml 47 53 47 53 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 345 347 345 347 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b012">12</xref>
###xml 348 350 348 350 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b035">35</xref>
###xml 351 353 351 353 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b036">36</xref>
###xml 354 357 354 357 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b103">103</xref>
###xml 358 361 358 361 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b104">104</xref>
###xml 431 440 431 440 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g010">Figure 10</xref>
###xml 455 461 455 461 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dbruce</italic>
###xml 497 499 497 499 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b012">12</xref>
(A) The model suggests that once an active Cul3Testis-Roc1b-Klhl10 E3 ubiquitin ligase complex is assembled, it recruits a caspase inhibitor "CI" protein (red) via the Kelch domain of the substrate recruitment protein Klhl10 (yellow). A candidate for this caspase inhibitor is dBruce, a giant BIR-domain-containing ubiquitin-conjugating enzyme [12,35,36,103,104]. dBruce can physically interact via its BIR domain with Klhl10 (see Figure 10), and loss of dbruce function leads to spermatid death [12]. Therefore, dBruce has biochemical and genetic properties expected for the postulated "CI" protein.
###end p 89
###begin p 90
(B) Next, the ubiquitin-conjugating enzyme (E2, blue), which is recruited by the RING finger protein Roc1b (purple), ubiquitinates the "CI" protein. (C) Subsequent degradation of this inhibitor allows the activation of caspases at the onset of spermatid individualization process.
###end p 90
###begin title 91
dBruce, a Giant IAP-Like Protein, Can Bind the Substrate-Recognition Protein Klhl10
###end title 91
###begin p 92
###xml 169 177 169 177 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g009">Figure 9</xref>
###xml 262 264 262 264 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b023">23</xref>
###xml 265 267 265 267 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b079">79</xref>
###xml 341 343 341 343 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b024">24</xref>
###xml 344 346 344 346 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b027">27</xref>
###xml 347 349 347 349 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b028">28</xref>
###xml 350 352 350 352 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b030">30</xref>
###xml 353 355 353 355 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b032">32</xref>
###xml 356 358 356 358 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b080">80</xref>
###xml 359 361 359 361 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b081">81</xref>
###xml 576 580 576 580 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3</italic>
###xml 676 682 676 682 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 682 685 682 685 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 672 685 672 685 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub><sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 696 699 696 699 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 690 699 690 699 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">klhl10<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 729 738 729 738 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g010">Figure 10</xref>
Our results suggest a simple working model in which the Cul3-Roc1b-Klhl10 complex promotes caspase activation via ubiquitination and degradation of a caspase inhibitor (Figure 9). The best-characterized family of endogenous caspase inhibitors is the IAP family [23,79]. Diap1 is essential for the survival of most, if not all somatic cells [24,27,28,30,32,80,81]. However, it appears that Diap1 is not the major caspase inhibitor in this context. If Diap1 was a substrate for Cullin-3-mediated protein degradation, we would have expected to see an increase of this protein in cul3 mutants. However, no significant differences in Diap1 protein levels between wild-type and cul3Testis-/- and klhl10-/- mutant testes were detected (Figure 10A).
###end p 92
###begin p 93
###xml 176 182 176 182 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dbruce</italic>
###xml 252 254 252 254 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b012">12</xref>
###xml 255 257 255 257 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b024">24</xref>
###xml 584 593 584 593 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g010">Figure 10</xref>
###xml 599 601 599 601 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g010">10</xref>
###xml 835 844 835 844 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g010">Figure 10</xref>
###xml 1028 1037 1028 1037 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g010">Figure 10</xref>
Another candidate is the giant, 4852-amino acid-long, IAP-like protein dBruce. dBruce function is necessary to protect sperm against unwanted caspase activity, because loss of dbruce function causes degeneration of spermatid nuclei and male sterility [12,24]. To further investigate possible interactions between dBruce and the Cul3-Roc1b-Klhl10 complex, we tested whether the substrate recruitment protein Klhl10 can bind to dBruce. For this purpose, we expressed tagged versions of Klhl10 and portions of dBruce in S2 cells and performed co-immunoprecipitation (co-IP) experiments (Figure 10B and 10C). In this system, Klhl10 efficiently immunoprecipitated both a dBruce "mini gene" (consisting of the first N-terminal 1,622 amino acids, including the BIR domain, and the last C-terminal 446 amino acids that contain the UBC domain; Figure 10B). Furthermore, a tagged peptide with the first N-terminal 387 amino acids of dBruce that includes the BIR domain (amino acids 251-321) is sufficient to bind to Klhl10 in this assay (Figure 10C). These data are consistent with the idea that dBruce is a substrate for the Cullin-3-based E3-ligase complex.
###end p 93
###begin title 94
Discussion
###end title 94
###begin p 95
###xml 157 167 157 167 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
###xml 324 326 324 326 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b012">12</xref>
###xml 327 329 327 329 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b050">50</xref>
###xml 1154 1156 1154 1156 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b012">12</xref>
###xml 1199 1207 1199 1207 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cullin-3</italic>
###xml 1679 1681 1679 1681 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b078">78</xref>
###xml 1682 1684 1682 1684 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b082">82</xref>
###xml 1685 1687 1685 1687 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b085">85</xref>
###xml 1944 1952 1944 1952 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g009">Figure 9</xref>
In the present study, we show a physiological requirement of a cullin-3-based E3-ubiqutin ligase complex for caspase activation and sperm differentiation in Drosophila. In this system, canonical apoptotic proteins are used to dramatically remodel cell structure by eliminating many organelles and the majority of cytoplasm [12,50]. Loss-of-function mutations in either a testis-specific isoform of cullin-3, the small RING protein Roc1b, or the BTB-Kelch protein Klhl10, all reduce or eliminate effector caspase activation in spermatids, are defective in spermatid individualization, and are male-sterile. Although mutations in many genes are known to affect male fertility, several observations indicate that the genes described here play a direct and important role in caspase regulation. First, only 3% of the male-sterile lines (33 out of 1,100) examined were negative for cleaved caspase-3 (CM1) staining, and many other mutants that block spermatid individualization and/or terminal differentiation remained caspase-positive. This confirms our earlier result that caspase activation in this system is independent of general differentiation events [12]. Secondly, mutations in any of the three cullin-3 complex genes retain AXO 49 staining, which has a temporal pattern of expression virtually identical with CM1-staining. This shows that the Cul3-Roc1b-Klhl10 complex is required for activation of effector caspase, but not for other individualization events, such as axonemal tubulin polyglycylation. Cullin-3-based E3 ubiquitin ligase complexes were previously implicated in various biological processes, including cell-cycle control and both Hedgehog and Wnt signaling [78,82-85]. However, a role of these proteins in caspase regulation has not yet been reported. A simple working model to explain our results is that the Cul3-Roc1b-Klhl10 complex promotes caspase activation via ubiquitination and degradation of a caspase inhibitor (Figure 9). This model is further supported by the findings that the Cullin-3-based complex and effector caspases are activated in a very similar spatiotemporal pattern in individualizing spermatids, which is consistent with a direct link between effector caspase activation and protein ubiquitination in this system.
###end p 95
###begin title 96
A Testis-Specific Cullin-3 Isoform Is Exclusively Expressed in the Male Germline
###end title 96
###begin p 97
###xml 29 37 29 37 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cullin-3</italic>
###xml 804 806 804 806 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b041">41</xref>
###xml 807 809 807 809 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b049">49</xref>
###xml 810 812 810 812 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b072">72</xref>
###xml 968 970 968 970 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b049">49</xref>
###xml 980 990 980 990 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
###xml 995 1001 995 1001 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 1151 1155 1151 1155 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 1226 1232 1226 1232 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 1337 1343 1337 1343 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 1333 1343 1333 1343 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 1343 1346 1343 1346 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1426 1432 1426 1432 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 1562 1568 1562 1568 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 1577 1581 1577 1581 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 1677 1687 1677 1687 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
###xml 1755 1764 1755 1764 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050251-sg003">Figure S3</xref>
###xml 1782 1797 1782 1797 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 1923 1925 1923 1925 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b086">86</xref>
###xml 1971 1977 1971 1977 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 1782 1797 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 1824 1829 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
We identified four different cullin-3 transcripts, three of which are somatic and share the same coding region, and one male germ-cell-specific transcript. The latter is transcribed from a separate promoter and contains a unique first exon that encodes the N-terminal TeNC domain. This result is somewhat surprising, because there have been no previous reports of tissue-specific expression of different Cullin isoforms with distinct biochemical and functional properties. Our results indicate that the testis-specific TeNC domain plays an important role for binding to the substrate recognition protein, Klhl10. The substrate specificity of Cullin-based E3 complexes is generally achieved through a variety of substrate recognition adaptors that may be differentially available in different cell types [41,49,72]. Similar to the SCF and ECS complexes, the BTB-containing substrate recognition proteins bind via their BTB domains to the N-terminal region of Cullin-3 [49]. In the Drosophila Cul3Testis isoform reported here, the TeNC domain is required for strong binding to Klhl10, caspase activation, spermatid individualization, and fertility. Cul3Soma, which lacks the TeNC domain but is otherwise nearly identical to Cul3Testis, bound much more weakly to Klhl10 and failed to rescue spermatid individualization and fertility of cul3Testis-/- flies. We conclude that the TeNC domain is important for proper binding of Cul3Testis to Klhl10. However, this domain is not sufficient for binding to Klhl10, indicating that additional sequences shared between Cul3Testis and Cul3Soma also contribute to this interaction. The TeNC domain is highly conserved among eight different Drosophila species with an evolutionary divergence of up to 40 million years (Figure S3). Spermatozoa of D. melanogaster are 300 times longer than human spermatozoa, and other Drosophilids can produce even longer sperm, with a length up to 6 cm [86]. It is possible that the TeNC domain of Cul3Testis evolved to facilitate coordinated regulation of caspase activation along the entire length of these giant spermatids. However, there is some indication that Cullin-3 can regulate caspases in tissues that do not contain a TeNC domain (see below). Therefore, it is possible that other factor(s) can substitute for the TeNC domain to promote the assembly of a similar Cullin-3-based E3 complex in species or tissues that do not express the TeNC domain.
###end p 97
###begin title 98
Diap1 Levels Are Not Affected in the Absence of the Functional Cul3-Roc1b-Klhl10 Complex, but dBruce Can Interact with the Substrate Recruitment Protein Klhl10 in S2 Cells
###end title 98
###begin p 99
###xml 50 54 50 54 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds1</sup>
###xml 46 54 46 54 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>mds1</sup></italic>
###xml 65 66 65 66 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sup>
###xml 59 66 59 66 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">klhl10<sup>3</sup></italic>
###xml 253 254 250 251 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">-</italic>
(A) Diap1 protein levels were not affected in cul3mds1 and klhl103 mutant testes, as assessed by Western blotting of protein extracts from dissected testes. Therefore, Diap1 does not appear to be a major target for the Cul3-based E3-ligase complex. beta-tubulin protein levels served as loading control.
###end p 99
###begin p 100
(B andC) Co-IP experiment in S2 cells indicate that Klhl10 can bind to the BIR domain of dBruce. The immunoprecipitate (IP) is shown at the top, and pre-incubation of whole lysates are shown at the bottom (Input). Cell lysates were incubated with IgG beads which bind to Protein A (PrA). For Western blotting of IPs, (B) anti-dBruce antibody or (C) anti-HA antibody were used.
###end p 100
###begin p 101
###xml 37 43 37 43 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dbruce</italic>
###xml 255 276 255 276 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
(B) Cells were co-transfected with a dbruce "mini gene" (consisting of the first N-terminal 1,622 amino acids, including the BIR domain, and the last C-terminal 446 amino acids that contain the UBC domain) and (lane 1) PrA-klhl10 or (lane 2) PrA-GFP (see Materials and Methods for details).
###end p 101
###begin p 102
###xml 241 262 241 262 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
(C) Cells were co-transfected with HA-tagged dBruce-BIR peptide containing the first N-terminal 387 amino acids of dBruce that includes the BIR domain region (amino acids 251-321). This motif is sufficient to bind to Klhl10 in S2 cells (see Materials and Methods for details).
###end p 102
###begin title 103
Role of the Ubiquitin-Proteasome System in Caspase Regulation and Cellular Remodeling
###end title 103
###begin p 104
###xml 172 174 172 174 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b037">37</xref>
###xml 175 177 175 177 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b087">87</xref>
###xml 178 180 178 180 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b091">91</xref>
###xml 357 359 357 359 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b078">78</xref>
###xml 360 362 360 362 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b082">82</xref>
###xml 363 365 363 365 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b085">85</xref>
###xml 659 664 659 664 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">drice</italic>
###xml 687 692 687 692 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dronc</italic>
###xml 712 716 712 716 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds1</sup>
###xml 708 716 708 716 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>mds1</sup></italic>
###xml 732 741 732 741 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050251-sg005">Figure S5</xref>
###xml 847 855 847 855 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g009">Figure 9</xref>
###xml 1144 1155 1144 1155 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila,</italic>
###xml 1320 1326 1320 1326 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 1316 1326 1316 1326 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 1326 1329 1326 1329 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1334 1340 1334 1340 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">klhl10</italic>
###xml 1340 1343 1340 1343 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;/&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1373 1382 1373 1382 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g010">Figure 10</xref>
###xml 1530 1539 1530 1539 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g010">Figure 10</xref>
###xml 1545 1547 1545 1547 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g010">10</xref>
###xml 1716 1722 1716 1722 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dbruce</italic>
###xml 1902 1904 1902 1904 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b012">12</xref>
###xml 1905 1907 1905 1907 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b024">24</xref>
Ubiquitin pathway proteins have well-established roles in the regulation of the cell cycle, DNA damage checkpoint, signal transduction, and in the regulation of apoptosis [37,87-91]. Cullin-3-based E3 ubiquitin ligase complexes were previously implicated in various biological processes, including cell-cycle control, Hedgehog signaling, and Wnt signaling [78,82-85]. Our current study points to a previously unknown link between the ubiquitin-proteasome protein degradation system and caspase activation during late spermatogenesis. It is unlikely that the Cullin-3-based complex regulates caspases at the mRNA level, because transcripts of effector caspase drice and initiator caspase dronc are present in cul3mds1 mutant testes (Figure S5). A more likely model is that the Cul3-Roc1b-Klhl10 complex promotes degradation of a caspase inhibitor (Figure 9). According to this model, the ubiquitination and degradation of this hypothetical caspase inhibitor at the onset of spermatid individualization would de-repress effector caspases and promote sperm differentiation. Whereas Diap1 is an essential caspase inhibitor in most somatic cells in Drosophila, it appears that it is not a major substrate for the Cul3-Roc1b-Klhl10 complex, because no significant differences in Diap1 protein levels between wild-type and cul3Testis-/- and klhl10-/- mutant testes were detected (Figure 10A). On the other hand, the BIR domain region of another IAP-like protein, dBruce, can bind to the substrate recruitment protein Klhl10 in S2 cells (Figure 10B and 10C). These results suggest that dBruce is at least one of the substrates for the Cullin-3-based E3-ligase complex. Importantly, it has been previously shown that loss of dbruce function causes degeneration of spermatid nuclei and male sterility, suggesting that dBruce function in spermatids is tightly controlled to prevent unrestrained caspase activity [12,24].
###end p 104
###begin p 105
###xml 447 449 447 449 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b014">14</xref>
###xml 450 452 450 452 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b051">51</xref>
###xml 590 592 590 592 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b014">14</xref>
###xml 593 595 593 595 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b051">51</xref>
###xml 596 598 596 598 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b054">54</xref>
###xml 716 718 716 718 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b053">53</xref>
###xml 1040 1042 1040 1042 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b092">92</xref>
Another interesting question raised by our results is how spermatids can survive high levels of apoptotic effector caspase activity. Since transgenic ectopic expression of the effector caspase drICE leads to spermatid death (EA, MB, HS, unpublished results), we propose that caspase activity in spermatids is restricted to specific subcellular compartments. A related phenomenon has been observed during the caspase-dependent pruning of neurites [14,51]. This process is similar to spermatid individualization in that it uses the apoptotic machinery for the destruction of parts of a cell [14,51-54]. Interestingly, a requirement for the ubiquitin-proteasome system in the process of axon pruning was also reported [53]. These similarities suggest that the processes of axon pruning and spermatid individualization may use similar mechanisms to restrain the activity of apoptotic proteins for cellular remodeling. In neurons, synaptic activity can lead to local remodeling of synaptic proteins by localized proteasome-mediated degradation [92]. Likewise, it is possible that the proposed caspase inhibitor is only locally degraded, which would allow for localized caspase activity in developing spermatids.
###end p 105
###begin p 106
###xml 122 130 122 130 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cullin-3</italic>
###xml 176 186 176 186 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
###xml 241 243 241 243 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b071">71</xref>
###xml 362 364 362 364 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b093">93</xref>
###xml 365 367 365 367 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b097">97</xref>
###xml 474 476 474 476 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b013">13</xref>
###xml 477 479 477 479 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b081">81</xref>
There is some evidence that the somatic isoforms of Cullin-3 may also regulate caspase activity in other tissues. Loss of cullin-3 function causes an increase in the number of Drosophila sensory organ precursors and external sensory organs [71]. This phenotype is reminiscent of decreased activity of the apoptotic proteins Ark, Dronc, Dcp-1, or cytochrome C-d [93-97]. Therefore, Cullin-3 may also play a role to regulate caspase activity in other non-apoptotic processes [13,81]. However, based on our results, we would expect that substrate recognition in the soma is mediated by proteins other than Klhl10.
###end p 106
###begin p 107
###xml 155 157 155 157 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b077">77</xref>
###xml 307 313 307 313 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">klhl10</italic>
###xml 384 386 384 386 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b098">98</xref>
###xml 505 511 505 511 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">klhl10</italic>
###xml 1045 1047 1045 1047 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b099">99</xref>
###xml 1048 1051 1048 1051 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b100">100</xref>
###xml 1098 1103 1098 1103 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sept4</italic>
###xml 1238 1240 1238 1240 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b099">99</xref>
###xml 1309 1315 1309 1315 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">klhl10</italic>
###xml 1352 1355 1352 1355 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b101">101</xref>
###xml 1462 1472 1462 1472 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
###xml 1621 1631 1621 1631 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
###xml 131 137 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">murine</span>
###xml 263 269 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">murine</span>
###xml 286 290 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 519 523 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 1092 1097 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1347 1350 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">men</span>
###xml 1692 1697 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
A recent report suggest that mammalian KLHL10 and Cullin-3 can interact in vitro and that Cullin-3 is highly expressed during late murine spermatogenesis [77]. In addition, KLHL10 was shown to be exclusively expressed in the cytoplasm of developmentally advanced murine spermatids, and mice carrying a null klhl10 allele are infertile due to defects during late spermatid maturation [98]. These data suggest that a similar E3 complex may function in late mammalian spermatogenesis and that the defects in klhl10 mutant mice may be due to lack of caspase-3 activity. Despite apparent anatomical differences between insect and mammalian spermiogenesis, there are similarities in the removal of bulk spermatid cytoplasm. Like in insects, intracellular bridges between spermatids and the bulk of the cytoplasm are eliminated during mammalian spermatogenesis. In addition, residual bodies, which contain the extruded cytoplasm of the mammalian spermatids show high levels of active caspase-3 expression and may be homologous to the insect waste bag [99,100]. Furthermore, targeted deletion of the mouse Sept4 locus, which encodes the pro-apoptotic protein ARTS, causes defects in the elimination of residual cytoplasm during sperm maturation [99]. Finally, a recent study reported a high frequency of mutations in klhl10 from infertile oligozoospermic men [101]. These intriguing anatomical and molecular similarities between spermatid individualization processes in Drosophila and mammals suggest that further studies on the link between the ubiquitin-proteasome system and apoptotic proteins during sperm differentiation in Drosophila may provide new insights into the etiology of some forms of human infertilities.
###end p 107

###begin p 111
###xml 25 31 25 31 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 21 31 21 31 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 122 126 122 126 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 118 126 118 126 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Soma</sub></italic>
The following BDGP's cul3Testis EST clones: AT08710, AT10339, AT08501, AT07783, AT21182, AT19493, and AT03216 and the cul3Soma EST clones SD20020 and RE58323 were either completely or partially sequenced, and some of them were used as templates in PCR reactions for subcloning.
###end p 111
###begin p 112
###xml 11 17 11 17 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 4 17 4 17 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tr-cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 29 33 29 33 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 22 33 22 33 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tr-cul3<sub>Soma</sub></italic>
###xml 185 191 185 191 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 181 191 181 191 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 316 319 316 319 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nsi</italic>
###xml 325 328 325 328 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Stu</italic>
###xml 490 493 490 493 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nhe</italic>
###xml 499 502 499 502 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Acc</italic>
###xml 585 588 585 588 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pst</italic>
###xml 592 595 592 595 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Stu</italic>
###xml 601 604 601 604 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Spe</italic>
###xml 608 611 608 611 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Acc</italic>
###xml 728 734 728 734 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 724 734 724 734 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 765 769 765 769 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 761 769 761 769 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Soma</sub></italic>
###xml 944 947 944 947 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xho</italic>
###xml 953 956 953 956 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nhe</italic>
###xml 1097 1100 1097 1100 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xho</italic>
###xml 1106 1109 1106 1109 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Nhe</italic>
###xml 1166 1169 1166 1169 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xho</italic>
###xml 1175 1178 1175 1178 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xba</italic>
###xml 1215 1221 1215 1221 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 1211 1221 1211 1221 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 1284 1290 1284 1290 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 1277 1290 1277 1290 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tr-cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 1302 1306 1302 1306 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 1295 1307 1295 1307 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tr-cul3<sub>Soma</sub>,</italic>
The tr-cul3Testis and tr-cul3Soma rescue constructs were generated as follows: a 979-bp fragment of the presumed promoter region and 5' UTR and a 345-bp fragment from the 3' UTR of cul3Testis were PCR amplified from genomic DNA (forward primer CACATTGGAGCATCGTTAAA and reverse primer GAGATTGCTACGCTGGTCCA with added NsiI and StuI restriction sites, respectively) and the BDGP's EST clone AT07783 (forward primer GGCCCACAAAAAGTAGCA and reverse primer AGAGAATATCAAGAAATATATTAGAGGG with added NheI and Acc65I restriction sites, respectively), and subcloned in a sequential order into the PstI + StuI and SpeI + Acc65I sites, respectively, of the CaSpeR-4 vector (from V. Pirrotta). Subsequently, the complete coding regions of cul3Testis (a 2,817-bp fragment) and cul3Soma (a 2,336-bp fragment) were PCR amplified from the BDGP's EST clones AT07783 (using the forward primer ATGCAAGGCCGCGATCCCCG and reverse primer TTAGGCCAAGTAGTTGTACA with added XhoI and NheI restriction sites, respectively) and SD20020 (using forward primer ATGAATCTGCGGGGAAATCC and reverse primer TTAGGCCAAGTAGTTGTACA with added XhoI and NheI restriction sites, respectively), and ligated into the XhoI and XbaI restrictions sites between the cul3Testis 5' and 3' UTRs within the CaSpeR-4 vector, to generate tr-cul3Testis and tr-cul3Soma, respectively.
###end p 112
###begin p 113
###xml 16 25 16 25 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tr-klhl10</italic>
###xml 55 61 55 61 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">klhl10</italic>
###xml 233 236 233 236 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sal</italic>
###xml 242 245 242 245 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xba</italic>
###xml 302 305 302 305 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xho</italic>
###xml 311 314 311 314 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xba</italic>
###xml 350 356 350 356 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 346 356 346 356 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
To generate the tr-klhl10 rescue construct, the ORF of klhl10 (a 2,320-bp fragment) was PCR amplified from the BDGP's EST clone AT19737 (using the forward primer ATGAGTCGTAATCAAAACG and reverse primer CTATGTACGACGACGAATTT with added SalI and XbaI restriction sites, respectively), and ligated into the XhoI and XbaI restriction sites between the cul3Testis 5' and 3' UTRs within the above vector.
###end p 113
###begin p 114
###xml 9 19 9 19 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
Standard Drosophila techniques were used to generate transgenic lines from these constructs.

###begin title 115
Genetic screen of the Zuker male-sterile collection lines.
###end title 115
###begin p 116
###xml 86 88 86 88 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b050">50</xref>
