###begin title 117
Antibody staining.
###end title 117
###begin p 118
###xml 110 112 110 112 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b012">12</xref>
###xml 122 128 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
###xml 214 217 <span type="species:ncbi:9685">Cat</span>
###xml 547 552 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 670 675 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Cleaved effector caspase antibody staining of young (0-2 d old) adult testes was carried out as described in [12] using a rabbit polyclonal anti-cleaved Caspase-3 (Asp175) antibody (CM1, Cell Signaling Technology, Cat. # 9661; ) diluted 1:75. The only changes are that the subsequent TRITC-phalloidin (Sigma; ) incubation for staining of the actin filaments was carried out for 5 min in room temperature, and the slides were subsequently rinsed twice for 10 min in PBS. Axonemal tubulin polyglycylation antibody staining was carried out using the mouse monoclonal antibody AXO 49 (a kind gift from Marie-Helene Bre, University of Paris-Sud, France) diluted 1:5,000. The mouse anti-multi ubiquitin monoclonal antibody (FK2, Stressgen; ) was used at a dilution of 1:100.
###end p 118
###begin title 119
Isolation of genomic DNA and sequencing of the mutant alleles.
###end title 119
###begin p 120
###xml 179 187 178 186 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cullin-3</italic>
###xml 191 197 190 196 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">klhl10</italic>
Genomic DNA was isolated from 25-50 adult flies using the High Pure PCR Template Preparation Kit (Roche; ). Genomic DNA (2 mug) was used to amplify overlapping fragments from the cullin-3 or klhl10 loci in wild-type and homozygote mutant lines. PCR reactions were carried out using DyNAzyme EXT DNA polymerase (Finnzymes; ), according to the manufacturer instructions. The products were purified using the High Pure PCR Product Purification Kit (Roche), concentrated by evaporation, and sequenced in a GENEWIZ sequencing facility.
###end p 120
###begin title 121
DEVDase activity assay.
###end title 121
###begin p 122
###xml 62 66 62 66 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds1</sup>
###xml 58 66 58 66 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>mds1</sup></italic>
###xml 558 562 554 555 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;</italic>
180 testes were dissected from newly eclosed wild-type or cul3mds1 homozygote males, collected into 0.5 mul standard skirted tubes (Fisherbrand #05-669-25; ), standing on ice and containing 70 mul of testis buffer (10 mM Tris-HCl [pH 6.8], 183 mM KCl, 47 mM NaCl, 1mM EDTA, and 1mM PMSF), homogenized using a Pellet Pestle Motor (Kontes; ), and subsequently transferred into three new tubes (30:30:10 mul). The tubes with 10 mul of the testes extracts were used for Western blot analysis to control for the protein amount in the samples by probing with anti-beta-tubulin antibody (E7; 1:1000; Hybridoma Bank; ). Either Z-VAD (20 muM final concentration; Enzyme Systems Products; ) or DMSO was added to each of the 30 mul tubes, and the samples were transferred to a 96-well assay white plate (Costar #3610, Corning; ), and allowed to incubate for 10 min at RT. Caspase-Glo 3/7 reagent (Promega; ) was added to a final volume of 200 mul and the signal was detected with a multiwell plate reader (SPECTRA max M2, Molecular Devices; ). Luminescence readings were obtained every 2 min; therefore, each time interval in the figure represents an average of five readings. Three experiments were performed that gave similar results.
###end p 122
###begin title 123
RNA isolation and RT-PCR.
###end title 123
###begin p 124
###xml 1500 1508 1453 1461 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 1583 1589 1536 1542 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 1579 1589 1532 1542 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 1760 1764 1713 1717 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 1756 1765 1709 1718 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Soma</sub>,</italic>
Total RNA was extracted by using the Micro-to-Midi Total RNA Purification System (Invitrogen; ) according to the manufacturer's recommendations. Ten-twenty young adult testes or male reproductive tracts and ten adult females were used to obtain enough RNA for 5-10 RT-PCR reactions. The samples were collected into 1.5-ml Eppendorf tubes that were standing on ice and containing 300 mul of the Invitrogen kit's lysis buffer and 3 mul of 2-mercaptoethanol, homogenized using a Pellet Pestle Motor (Kontes), and subsequently purified using the same kit. In cases when the genomic DNA had to be removed, the 30 mul of the RNA was incubated with 4 mul of RQ1 DNase and 3.8 mul of appropriate buffer (Promega; ) for 1.5 h at 37 degreesC, and subsequently purified again with the Invitrogen kit. The RNA was stored in -80 degreesC or immediately used for RT-PCR reactions using the SuperScriptTM III One-Step RT-PCR System with Platinums Taq DNA polymerase (Invitrogen). The Mastercycler Gradient PCR machine (Eppendorf; ) was programmed as follows: 50 degreesC for 30 min for the RT step followed by 94 degreesC for 2 min, and the amplification steps of 94 degreesC for 30 s, 60 degreesC for 30 s, and 68 degreesC for 1 min. A master-mix was prepared and aliquoted to five tubes, each of which was amplified for 17, 20, 25, 30, or 35 cycles. Absence of genomic DNA in RNA preparations was verified by replacing the RT/Taq mix with only Taq DNA polymerase (Invitrogen). The comparative RT-PCR reactions in Figure 3 were performed using two pairs of primers in a same reaction mix: For cul3Testis the forward primer TCTCATGCAAGGCCGCGATC and the reverse primer CGGGTTATTGGCTGGCGGTC amplified a 2,997-bp cDNA fragment (and a 3,715-bp genomic fragment), whereas for cul3Soma, the forward primer CATTGATTGCCGCCGAGGAA and the reverse primer CGGGTTATTGGCTGGCGGTC amplified a 2,642-bp cDNA fragment (and a 4,911-bp genomic fragment).
###end p 124
###begin p 125
###xml 66 72 66 72 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 59 72 59 72 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tr-cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 113 121 113 121 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 285 289 285 289 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 278 289 278 289 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tr-cul3<sub>Soma</sub></italic>
###xml 293 301 293 301 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0050251-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 362 368 362 368 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 358 368 358 368 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub></italic>
###xml 441 445 441 445 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 437 445 437 445 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Soma</sub></italic>
###xml 524 530 524 530 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 520 531 520 531 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sub>Testis</sub>,</italic>
For amplification of the 868-bp fragment of the transgenic tr-cul3Testis (and the 858-bp endogenous fragment) in Figure 4B, the forward primer GAGACCCGAATCGCGAGTAG and the reverse primer GCATTCTTTAAGCTGGCCCA were used. For amplification of the 335-bp fragment of the transgenic tr-cul3Soma in Figure 4C, the forward primer GAGACCCGAATCGCGAGTAG (specific for cul3Testis promoter) and the reverse primer CATTTTGCCCTCCTTCTTGG (specific for cul3Soma) were used. To simultaneously amplify a 496-bp fragment of the endogenous cul3Testis, the reverse primer GGAGGCGTTGGGCACATTGA was also used in the same reaction.
###end p 125
###begin p 126
###xml 46 51 46 51 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">drice</italic>
###xml 60 69 60 69 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050251-sg005">Figure S5</xref>
###xml 213 218 213 218 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dronc</italic>
###xml 227 236 227 236 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="pbio-0050251-sg005">Figure S5</xref>
For amplification of the 538-bp fragment from drice mRNA in Figure S5A, the forward primer GCCCACCTTGAAGTCTCGCG and the reverse primer CAGGATGTCCAGCCGCTTGC were used. For amplification of the 527-bp fragment from dronc mRNA in Figure S5B, the forward primer CCACCGCCTATAACCTGCTG and the reverse primer CTGCACATACGACGAGGAGG were used.
###end p 126
###begin title 127
###xml 22 27 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
Plasmid construction, yeast strains, and cDNA library screening.
###end title 127
###begin p 128
###xml 8 14 8 14 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 23 27 23 27 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 119 125 119 125 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 277 280 277 280 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Eco</italic>
###xml 287 290 287 290 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pst</italic>
###xml 376 380 376 380 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Soma</sub>
###xml 534 537 534 537 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Eco</italic>
###xml 544 547 544 547 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pst</italic>
###xml 653 656 653 656 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Eco</italic>
###xml 663 666 663 666 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pst</italic>
###xml 938 941 938 941 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Eco</italic>
###xml 948 951 948 951 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bgl</italic>
###xml 1051 1054 1051 1054 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Eco</italic>
###xml 1061 1064 1061 1064 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bam</italic>
The Cul3Testis and Cul3Soma "bait" constructs were generated as follows: a 2,817-bp fragment containing the entire Cul3Testis coding region was PCR amplified from the BDGP's EST clone AT19493 (forward primer CAAGGCCGCGATCCCCG and reverse primer TTAGGCCAAGTAGTTGTACA with added EcoRI and PstI restriction sites, respectively), and a 2,336-bp fragment containing the entire Cul3Soma coding region was PCR amplified from the BDGP's EST clone SD20020 (forward primer AATCTGCGGGGAAATCCTC and reverse primer TTAGGCCAAGTAGTTGTACA with added EcoRI and PstI restriction sites, respectively). Both were subcloned in frame to the GAL4 DNA-binding domain using the EcoRI and PstI sites of the pGBKT7 vector (Matchmaker, Clontech; ). For the TeNC domain "bait" construct, a 600-bp fragment containing the entire TeNC ORF was PCR amplified from wild-type genomic DNA (forward primer CAAGGCCGCGATCCCCG and reverse primer GGGATATTAAGACTTTCGCT with added EcoRI and BglII restriction sites, respectively) and subcloned in frame to the GAL4 DNA binding domain using the EcoRI and BamHI sites of the pGBKT7 vector (Matchmaker, Clontech).
###end p 128
###begin p 129
###xml 40 64 40 64 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Saccharomyces cerevisiae</named-content>
###xml 91 101 91 101 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
###xml 40 64 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">Saccharomyces cerevisiae</span>
###xml 361 366 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
Two hybrid screens were performed using Saccharomyces cerevisiae strain AH109 and an adult Drosophila cDNA library (Matchmaker, Clontech). Selection was accomplished on synthetic complete medium lacking tryptophan, leucine, and adenine for 3-7 d at 30 degreesC. To test for LacZ activity, positive "prey" cDNA clones were isolated and transformed into the Y187 yeast strain, which was pre-transformed with the appropriate "bait" constructs.
###end p 129
###begin p 130
###xml 8 14 8 14 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dbruce</italic>
###xml 167 170 167 170 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Eco</italic>
###xml 177 180 177 180 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xho</italic>
###xml 239 242 239 242 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Eco</italic>
###xml 249 252 249 252 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xho</italic>
###xml 300 306 300 306 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dbruce</italic>
###xml 438 441 438 441 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sal</italic>
###xml 447 450 447 450 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xba</italic>
###xml 591 594 591 594 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Cla</italic>
###xml 679 682 679 682 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xho</italic>
###xml 688 691 688 691 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xba</italic>
###xml 710 716 710 716 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dbruce</italic>
###xml 747 753 747 753 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dbruce</italic>
The UAS-dbruce "mini gene" was generated as follows: a 5,022-bp fragment encoding the N-terminal 1,622 amino acids of dBruce (including the BIR domain) was cleaved by EcoRI and XhoI from the BDGP's EST clone LD31268 and subcloned into the EcoRI and XhoI sites of the pUASt vector to generate the UAS-dbruce-5' vector. Next, a 1,990-bp fragment encoding the C-terminal 446 amino acids of dBruce (including the UBC domain) was cleaved with SalI and XbaI from clone T1A-ClaI (originally identified as clone T1A in the T. Hazelrigg testis cDNA library by J. Agapite and was further cleaved with ClaI to remove the first 357 bp and then self ligated), and subcloned in frame into the XhoI and XbaI sites of the UAS-dbruce-5' vector to generate the UAS-dbruce "mini gene" plasmid.
###end p 130
###begin title 131
Western blotting of adult testis, antibodies, and immunoprecipitation.
###end title 131
###begin p 132
###xml 385 388 384 387 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b102">102</xref>
###xml 421 423 420 422 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b030">30</xref>
###xml 312 317 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 369 372 <span type="species:ncbi:9685">cat</span>
###xml 393 399 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
Forty to sixty testes from wild-type and mutant adult males were used to prepare extracts in 30 mul of cell lysis buffer (20 mM HEPES-KOH [pH 7.6], 150 mM NaCl, 10% glycerol, 1% Triton X-100, 2 mM EDTA, 1x protease inhibitor cocktail, and 1 mM DTT). Total protein was used for Western blot analysis using either mouse anti-CUL-3 (1:1,000; BD Transduction Laboratories, cat #611848; ) [102] or rabbit anti-Diap1 antibody [30].
###end p 132
###begin p 133
###xml 156 159 156 159 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Sal</italic>
###xml 165 168 165 168 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xma</italic>
###xml 195 198 195 198 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xho</italic>
###xml 204 207 204 207 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xma</italic>
###xml 375 376 375 376 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sub>
###xml 470 473 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rat</span>
To generate the anti-dBruce antibody, sequence encoding the C-terminal 446 amino acids of dBruce was cleaved from the T1A-ClaI cDNA clone (see above) using SalI and XmaI and then cloned into the XhoI and XmaI sites of a derivative plasmid of the pET14b (Novagen; ). The expression plasmid was then transformed into BL21/DE3/pLys, followed by 2-h IPTG induction to express His6-dBruce-C-term. This protein was purified by nickel affinity chromatography and used to raise rat polyclonal antibody (Covance; ). This antibody recognizes the dBruce "mini gene" band on a Western blot (1:1,000).
###end p 133
###begin p 134
###xml 75 80 75 80 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Gal4,</italic>
###xml 85 96 85 96 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PrA-klhl10,</italic>
###xml 112 118 112 118 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dbruce</italic>
###xml 138 152 138 152 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HA-(dbruce)BIR</italic>
###xml 237 244 237 244 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PrA-GFP</italic>
###xml 260 270 260 270 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PrA-klhl10</italic>
###xml 389 395 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
For immunoprecipitation reactions, S2 cells were co-transfected with Actin-Gal4, UAS-PrA-klhl10, and either UAS-dbruce "mini gene" or UAS-HA-(dbruce)BIR plasmids. For negative controls, S2 cells were co-transfected as above but with UAS-PrA-GFP instead of UAS-PrA-klhl10. Cells were lysed 48 h post-transfection, and the extracts were then incubated with Dynabeads which are conjugated to rabbit IgG (Dynal, Invitrogen) at 4 degreesC for 1.5 h. Bound proteins were eluted by boiling in 3 x SDS loading buffer and detected with anti-dBruce antibody (for the presence of dBruce "mini gene") or anti-HA antibody (for the presence of HA-(dBruce)BIR).
###end p 134
###begin title 135
Supporting Information
###end title 135
###begin title 136
The Spatiotemporal Expression Patterns of Axonemal Tubulin Polyglycylation and Effector Caspase Activation at the Onset of Spermatid Individualization Are Identical
###end title 136
###begin p 137
###xml 116 118 116 118 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0050251-b066">66</xref>
(A-D) Quadruple staining of wild-type spermatids with the anti-glycylated tubulin monoclonal antibody AXO 49 (red, [66]); CM1, which detects cleaved caspase-3 (green); phalloidin, which marks the individualization complex (IC, magenta); and DAPI, to visualize the nuclei (blue). (A) Red layer, (B) green layer, (C) magenta and blue layers, and (D) all 4 layers. Before or at the early assembly of an IC, neither tubulin polyglycylation nor cleaved caspase-3 is detected (yellow arrowhead). Once a mature IC is formed at the vicinity of the nuclei and is about to begin its caudal translocation, steep cascades of both tubulin polyglycylation on the axoneme and cleaved caspase-3 expression in the cytoplasm are observed from the nuclei to the tip of the tails (green arrowheads).
###end p 137
###begin p 138
(A-G) When the IC moves caudally and the bulk cytoplasm of the spermatids accumulates in a cystic bulge (CB, white arrowheads), cleaved caspase-3 is removed from the post-individualized portion of the spermatids (the region between the nuclei and the CB, yellow arrows), but it is still prominent within the CB and the pre-individualized region (the region between the CB and the tip of the tail, white arrows). Cleaved caspase-3 is eventually eliminated from mature spermatozoa. On the other hand, polyglycylation of the axonemal tubulin persists during spermatid individualization and in mature spermatozoa (green arrowhead, yellow arrows and data not shown). Scale bars in (A-D), 100 mum; in (E and F), 40 mum; and in (G), 200 mum.
###end p 138

###begin title 141
###xml 15 19 15 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds1</italic>
Mapping of the mds1 Mutation
###end title 141
###begin p 142
The thick bar represents the cytological region between 35B1 and 35F7. The relative nucleotide positions of this region within the second chromosome are indicated above the bar. Thin bars depict available deficiencies in this region (red flanked by gray, Bloomington's deficiencies; green, DrosDel's deficiency; blue, Exelixis' deficiencies).
###end p 142
###begin p 143
###xml 4 8 4 8 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds1</italic>
###xml 177 179 177 179 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Df</italic>
###xml 182 193 182 193 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">)TE35BC-24,</italic>
###xml 311 315 311 315 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds1</italic>
###xml 362 366 362 366 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds1</italic>
###xml 488 490 488 490 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Df</italic>
###xml 502 504 502 504 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Df</italic>
###xml 597 601 597 601 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds1</italic>
###xml 650 654 650 654 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds1</italic>
###xml 724 727 724 727 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gft</italic>
###xml 748 751 748 751 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">nht</italic>
###xml 824 828 824 828 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mds1</italic>
###xml 832 840 832 840 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cullin-3</italic>
The mds1 mutants were crossed to all the deficiency lines from FlyBase's second chromosome "kit" and the trans-heterozygotes were tested for male fertility. The deficiency line Df(2L)TE35BC-24, which contains a large chromosomal deletion (cytological region 35B4/6-35E1/2) failed to complement the sterility of mds1 males, suggesting that this region covers the mds1 mutation. Additional smaller deletion lines in this region were subsequently analyzed. The deficiencies shown in purple, Df(2L)ED3 and Df(2L)Exel8034, failed to complement, whereas the deficiencies shown in black complemented the mds1 sterility. This genetic analysis restricted the mds1 mutation to a 54-kb genomic interval comprising nine genes (from the gft gene in 35C1 to the nht gene in 35D1). See details in the main text on the final mapping of the mds1 to cullin-3.
###end p 143

###begin title 146
###xml 53 63 53 63 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
The TeNC Domain Has Been Highly Conserved Throughout Drosophila Phylogeny
###end title 146
###begin p 147
###xml 24 30 24 30 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Testis</sub>
###xml 42 52 42 52 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Drosophila</named-content>
###xml 108 121 108 121 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">melanogaster;</italic>
###xml 128 137 128 137 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">simulans;</italic>
###xml 144 151 144 151 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">yakuba;</italic>
###xml 158 165 158 165 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">erecta;</italic>
###xml 172 182 172 182 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ananassae;</italic>
###xml 189 203 189 203 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pseudoobscura;</italic>
###xml 210 221 210 221 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mojavensis;</italic>
###xml 228 235 228 235 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">virilis</italic>
###xml 752 767 752 767 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. melanogaster</named-content>
###xml 772 785 772 785 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. mojavensis</named-content>
###xml 789 799 789 799 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">D. virilis</named-content>
###xml 752 767 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 772 785 <span type="species:ncbi:7230">D. mojavensis</span>
###xml 789 799 <span type="species:ncbi:7244">D. virilis</span>
The TeNC domains of Cul3Testis from eight Drosophila species were aligned using the ClustalW program (Dmel, melanogaster; Dsim, simulans; Dyak, yakuba; Dere, erecta; Dana, ananassae; Dpse, pseudoobscura; Dmoj, mojavensis; Dvir, virilis). Identical or similar amino acids are depicted by the same color. In the consensus (cons.) lines, asterisks represent residues that are identical in all the species. Square dots appear above every tenth residue, and the total numbers of amino acid in each domain appear on the right of every line in the final block. Although conservation appears throughout the domain, two regions of high conservation in the beginning and in the very end of the domain are revealed. Note that the divergence time distance between D. melanogaster and D. mojavensis or D. virilis is 40 million years.
###end p 147

###xml 801 808 801 808 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cul3<sup>&#8722;/&#8722;</sup></italic>

Koshland Career Development Chair and is supported by an Alon Fellowship at the Weizmann Institute of Science. EA also acknowledges The Morasha Program of The Israel Science Foundation for its support. HS is an Investigator with the Howard Hughes Medical Institute.
